# Consultation 45 — M11 alignment audit + integration-guide rewrite

Two asks in one pass. They share context.

## Ask 1 — alignment audit

Review consultation 35 (UX direction), consultation 36 (hostPreview
contract), and every phase review (37–44). Then walk the M11.0
through M11.7 commit ladder and confirm each delivered piece matches
the original agreement, OR call out where it drifted.

The relevant commits:

```
M11    base — lottery dogfood end-to-end (the pre-UX work)
M11.1  hostPreview contract + inbox preview/detail split  + review 37
M11.2  read state + M7 CAS cross-device sync              + review 38
M11.3  bottom nav + date buckets + archive                + review 39
M11.4  bundle-by-hash + revocation classification         + review 40
M11.5  host-side metadata search                          + review 41
M11.6  relative timestamps + delete + hide revoked devs   + review 43
M11.7  multi-select + group-by-sender                     + review 44
```

The original UX direction came out of consultation 35 with this
agreed shape:

- inbox-first app that hosts micro-apps in detail surfaces
- preview/detail master/detail pattern; native host rows, plugin
  owns detail render
- read state local-first, synced via M7 CAS blob
- date buckets, no plugin grouping by default in V1 (consultation
  35 specifically argued against plugin grouping as primary nav —
  later phases added it as an OPTIONAL toggle)
- host-owned metadata search, plugin-scoped content search V1.5
- bottom nav (Inbox / Senders / Settings)
- archive vs delete vs dismiss as distinct concepts
- bundle-by-hash retention so render history survives plugin updates
- revocation classification (superseded / compromised / sender_disabled)
- 4 V1.5 deferrals: plugin dashboards, plugin-scoped search,
  cross-plugin search aggregation, plugin-owned chrome

Specifically pressure-test:

1. **Group-by-sender ended up shipped (M11.7) even though consultation
   35 argued against it.** Reconcile: did we drift, or was the
   "user requested it as a toggle" exception acceptable?

2. **Bundle-by-hash retention.** Consultation 35 said old messages
   must render against the bundle they were validated for. M11.4
   added bundle-by-hash caching but acknowledged in-memory only;
   M11.4 fix-ups switched to `/by-id` lookup. Is the V1 state
   (in-memory cache, no disk persistence, restart loses the cache
   but `/by-id` re-resolves to the original row) compatible with
   the original spec, or did we underdeliver?

3. **`hostPreview` schema vs consultation 36.** Final contract has
   title (required) + subtitle + summary + searchText. No priority,
   category, timestamp, or accessibilityLabel — all explicitly cut
   in consultation 36. Confirm we shipped exactly that contract,
   not a drift.

4. **Read-mark trigger.** Consultations 35/38 said "open detail
   view only, NOT scroll-into-view." M11.2 wired it that way.
   Confirm.

5. **Archive durability.** M11.3 archive kdoc was rewritten to
   honestly say "hide-from-active while server still has the
   message" rather than the original consultation-35 promise of
   "keep past server expiry." M11.4 onwards did NOT add local body
   storage. Is the V1 framing acceptable, or did the original
   spec really require local persistence?

6. **Delete vs dismiss vs archive.** Three distinct concepts in
   consultation 35. We shipped:
   - Archive (local + synced, hide from inbox + visible in archive)
   - Delete (local + synced, hide from inbox AND archive)
   - Dismiss (server endpoint exists, NOT wired from client UI)
   Did we honor the trinary?

7. **The four V1.5 deferrals** named in consultation 35 — were
   they all preserved (i.e. we didn't quietly ship one), or were
   any of them partially built and now constitute "half a feature"?

8. **Any commits whose diff doesn't match what their review
   asked for.** Sanity check that each "address review N" commit
   actually contains the fix it claims.

Output: green/yellow/red per phase against its original consultation
intent, with one-line justifications. Where it's yellow or red,
suggest the minimum delta to make it green.

## Ask 2 — integration-guide rewrite

I started a rewrite of `docs/integration-guide.md` to give to
lottery-Claude (the sender-side dev). The user's instruction was:

> the md shouldn't be saying "we changed this to that" it should be
> as currently describe the thing without before and after

Current state of the file: HEAD checkout of `docs/integration-
guide.md`. I've added a "What the host does for you" subsection to
§1 that lists native row rendering / read sync / date buckets /
group toggle / search / archive / delete / multi-select / bottom
nav / revocation UX, all framed as current behavior.

What I haven't done yet:

- A new **§5.5 Revoking a plugin version** describing the
  `client.revoke_plugin(plugin_row_id, reason=...)` method I just
  added to sdk-python, the four reason enums, and the host's UX
  per reason.
- A new **§10 Versioning + history** describing the bundle-by-hash
  guarantee (so senders know they can ship a v2 without breaking
  v1 messages already in users' inboxes).
- Scrub of any remaining "now" / "is no longer" / "we changed"
  phrasing that frames things as diffs from a previous state.

Review the file as it stands AND the planned additions above.
Identify:

- Any current-state claim that's actually wrong (mismatched against
  the M11.x code).
- Any sender-facing API or behavior that's NOT documented but
  should be.
- Any wording that smuggles changelog framing.
- Any field cap, error message, or example payload that doesn't
  match the actual implementation.

Output the specific delta you'd apply (file edits, not free-form
prose) so the user can hand the result to lottery-Claude with
confidence.

# Syncler integration guide

You are integrating your app with the Syncler platform. Syncler is a content-blind transport + plugin host: your backend pushes encrypted blobs to a user's phone, and a JavaScript plugin you wrote renders them and handles taps. **Read this end-to-end before writing code; it's ~7 pages.**

Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code, your callback endpoint ג€” Syncler just routes bytes.

## 1. What you're building

Two artifacts:

1. A **JavaScript plugin** that runs in the Syncler Android app's WebView and renders the **detail view** of a card when the user taps it. The plugin defines buttons that POST back to your backend.
2. **Backend code** that pushes a card to the user via the Syncler server, and an HTTP endpoint that receives the action callback.

The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message ג€” sender name, title, subtitle, summary, relative timestamp. The host draws that row from structured metadata you embed in the payload (`hostPreview`, ֲ§2). The plugin's `render()` is reserved for the full-screen detail view that appears when the user taps a row.

### What the host does for you

Once a card is in a user's inbox, the host handles all of the following without you doing anything plugin-side:

- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary / timestamp).
- **Unread indicator** + read sync across the user's devices. A row marks read when the user opens the detail view; the state syncs via an encrypted CAS state blob.
- **Date buckets** in the chronological view (Today / Yesterday / Earlier).
- **Group-by-sender** toggle with collapsible sections ג€” the user picks chronological or grouped from the top app bar.
- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
- **Archive** + **Delete** + **Multi-select** with bulk Archive / Delete. Archive/delete state is local and synced across devices; deleted messages are hidden from inbox AND archive.
- **Bottom navigation** (Inbox / Senders / Settings) ג€” the user is always one tap away from your card.
- **Revocation UX** ג€” if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See ֲ§5.5.

You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.

## 2. Protocol

### Payload (your backend ג†’ user device)

Two parts: a reserved **`hostPreview`** block the platform renders natively as the inbox row, and the rest of the payload that your plugin's `render()` consumes for the detail view.

```json
{
  "hostPreview": {
    "title": "Something happened",
    "subtitle": "Account A ג€¢ 12 minutes ago",
    "summary": "Brief one-sentence context for the row.",
    "searchText": ["account-a", "alert", "threshold"]
  },
  "item_id": "<your-internal-id>",
  "body": "Details for the detail view, used by render()",
  "action_label": "Acknowledge"
}
```

That JSON is your `payload` argument to `client.send_to(...)`. The plugin's `render(payload)` receives the entire dict ג€” including the `hostPreview` block ג€” but it doesn't need to use it (the host already drew the row).

**`hostPreview` contract** (validated by `client.send_to` ג€” invalid blocks raise at send time):

| Field | Required | Type | Cap |
|---|---|---|---|
| `title` | yes | string | 80 UTF-8 bytes |
| `subtitle` | no | string | 120 UTF-8 bytes |
| `summary` | no | string | 240 UTF-8 bytes |
| `searchText` | no | string[] | 16 entries ֳ— 64 UTF-8 bytes each |

Total serialized `hostPreview` ג‰₪ 2048 UTF-8 bytes. Missing block ג†’ the row falls back to *"New message from {sender_name}"*. Senders **should** include it.

`searchText` is folded into the host's inbox search alongside title, subtitle, summary, and sender name. The host does a case-insensitive substring match ג€” populate this with the terms a user would type into the search box but that aren't part of the visible row (ticker symbols, ticket numbers, account references). Plugin-scoped *content* search (a search bar that runs against your backend) is V1.5.

### Action callback (user ג†’ your backend)

When the user taps an action button in your plugin, the plugin POSTs to your declared endpoint with whatever body your `onclick` handler builds:

```
POST https://your-app.example.com/api/action
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "item_id": "...",
  "acted_at": "2026-05-20T14:30:00Z"
}
```

The platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body in V1 ג€” see ֲ§7 for the full contract. Idempotency is your responsibility: dedupe by `item_id` (or a sender-generated identifier you echo back) because the platform may double-deliver under retry.

## 3. Plugin code

`src/plugin.ts`:

```ts
import {
  BasePlugin,
  DismissBehavior,
  registerPlugin,
  type HostPreview,
  type PluginManifest,
} from '@syncler/plugin-sdk';

interface MyPayload {
  // hostPreview is in every payload your plugin receives ג€” the host already
  // drew the inbox row from it, but render() can still use it (e.g. to repeat
  // the title in the detail header).
  hostPreview: HostPreview;
  item_id: string;
  body: string;
  action_label: string;
}

class MyPlugin extends BasePlugin {
  static manifest: PluginManifest = {
    id: 'com.example.myapp',         // your plugin_identifier
    name: 'My App',
    version: '1.0.0',
    senderId: '<your-sender-id>',    // the UUID Syncler issued you
    bundleHash: '<set by sign-bundle.ts>',
    signature: '<set by sign-bundle.ts>',
    declaredCapabilities: ['network'],
    declaredEndpoints: ['https://your-app.example.com/api/*'],
    dismissBehavior: DismissBehavior.DISMISS_ALL,
    minPlatformVersion: '1.0.0',
  };

  // onMessage is NOT invoked in V1 inbox mode ג€” message arrival is already
  // surfaced by the host-rendered row from hostPreview. If you implement it
  // anyway, do not call platform.showNotification (rejects in V1).
  // The host will invoke onMessage when the V1.5 OS-notification path ships.

  render(payload: MyPayload): string {
    // V1 recommended pattern: button handler calls `platform.network.fetch`
    // directly. The `platform.message.respond` + `onAction` round-trip is
    // reserved for V1.5 (it lets the platform sync action state across
    // devices). For V1, post directly to your declared endpoint.
    return `
      <div style="font-family:sans-serif;padding:16px">
        <h2>${escapeHtml(payload.hostPreview.title)}</h2>
        <p>${escapeHtml(payload.body)}</p>
        <button id="act" style="font-size:18px;padding:12px">${escapeHtml(payload.action_label)}</button>
      </div>
      <script>
        const itemId = ${JSON.stringify(payload.item_id)};
        document.getElementById('act').onclick = async () => {
          await platform.network.fetch('https://your-app.example.com/api/action', {
            method: 'POST',
            headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
            body: JSON.stringify({
              item_id: itemId,
              acted_at: new Date().toISOString(),
            }),
          });
          document.getElementById('act').textContent = 'Sent';
        };
      </script>
    `;
  }
}

// Required: self-register at bundle load. Without this call the host's
// dispatcher has no plugin to dispatch into, and you'll see a "missing
// registerPlugin() call?" error in the card.
registerPlugin(new MyPlugin());
```

Render whatever HTML/CSS/JS suits your domain. The WebView is isolated; only `platform.*` APIs cross the boundary.

**V1 card-render bridge ג€” what's wired:**
- `platform.network.fetch(url, init)` ג€” works, gated by `declaredEndpoints` glob match
- `platform.showNotification`, `platform.storage`, `platform.camera`, `platform.gallery`, `platform.file`, `platform.location`, `platform.message.respond` ג€” *reject* with a clear error in V1 inbox mode. The full bridge needs the multi-process plugin host and is a follow-up. For V1 dogfood, stick to network.fetch.

## 4. Build + sign the plugin

```sh
# Install the SDK
cd my-plugin
npm install @syncler/plugin-sdk

# Build ג€” IIFE format, NOT ESM. The host loads the bundle inside a regular
# `<script>` tag, which can't parse `export` statements.
npx esbuild src/plugin.ts \
  --bundle \
  --format=iife \
  --global-name=SynclerPluginExports \
  --platform=browser \
  --outfile=dist/plugin.bundle.js

# Sign it (positional args, tsx is required for the TS tool):
npx tsx node_modules/@syncler/plugin-sdk/tools/sign-bundle.ts \
  dist/plugin.bundle.js \
  ~/.syncler/keys/sender.pem \
  manifest.json \
  manifest.signed.json
```

The tool signs the canonical-manifest-with-bundleHash-bytes (the exact bytes the Android host verifies against ג€” see `docs/crypto-spec.md` ֲ§5). `manifest.signed.json` will contain populated `bundleHash` + `signature` fields.

Host the bundle file at a stable HTTPS URL (CDN, S3, GitHub raw). For local development, debug builds of the Android app also accept plain `http://` URLs (e.g. a Python `-m http.server` on your LAN). Release builds require HTTPS.

## 5. Publishing the plugin (your backend, one time per version)

```python
from syncler import Client
import hashlib, json

client = Client(
    sender_name="My App",
    private_key_path="~/.syncler/keys/sender.pem",
    base_url="https://api.syncler.app",
)
client.set_sender_id("<the sender_id Syncler issued you>")

bundle = open("dist/plugin.bundle.js", "rb").read()
manifest = json.loads(open("manifest.signed.json").read())

response = client.publish_plugin(
    plugin_identifier="com.example.myapp",
    version="1.0.0",
    manifest_hash=hashlib.sha256(json.dumps(
        {k: v for k, v in manifest.items() if k != "signature"},
        sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")
    ).encode()).digest(),
    bundle_hash=hashlib.sha256(bundle).digest(),
    bundle_signature=bytes.fromhex(manifest["signature"]),
    signed_bundle_url="https://your-app.example.com/syncler-plugin.bundle.js",
    capabilities=["network"],
    endpoints=["https://your-app.example.com/api/*"],
)

print("Published row:", response["plugin_row_id"])
# Save this ג€” you'll need it in `send_to(plugin_id=...)`.
```

## 6. Sending a card (your backend, per event)

```python
# After pairing ג€” see SDK README for the pairing dance.
client.set_pairing(user_id="...", pairing_key=b"...32-bytes...")

result = client.send_to(
    user_uuid=user_uuid,
    plugin_identifier="com.example.myapp",
    plugin_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
    payload={
        "hostPreview": {
            "title": "Something happened",
            "subtitle": "Account A",
            "summary": "Brief one-sentence context.",
            "searchText": ["account-a", "alert"],
        },
        "item_id": "abc-123",
        "body": "Details for the detail view.",
        "action_label": "Acknowledge",
    },
    min_plugin_version="1.0.0",
)
```

## 7. The action callback endpoint

`https://your-app.example.com/api/action` accepts whatever body your plugin's `onclick` handler POSTs. In the example above that's:

```http
POST /api/action
Content-Type: application/json

{ "item_id": "...", "acted_at": "..." }
```

Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and have the plugin echo it back. Dedupe by `item_id` alone if a single tap is what you care about.

- Status 200 -> recorded.
- Status 409 -> idempotent dedupe (already saw this item); platform may retry on transient network errors so be ready.
- Status 4xx other -> platform surfaces a generic failure to the plugin's promise.

```python
# Flask example ג€” dedupe by item_id alone in V1.
@app.post("/api/action")
def action():
    data = request.json
    item_id = data["item_id"]
    if Action.query.filter_by(item_id=item_id).first():
        return "", 409
    db.session.add(Action(item_id=item_id, acted_at=data["acted_at"]))
    db.session.commit()
    return "", 200
```

## 8. Testing it end-to-end

1. Install the Syncler Android app (`./gradlew :app:installDebug`).
2. Sign up + log in. The app auto-enrolls this device with the server.
3. From your backend, run a script that registers your sender and prints a pairing QR (see SDK README).
4. Tap **Pair sender** ג†’ **Scan QR** in the Syncler app. Confirm the fingerprint matches what your script prints.
5. After confirming, the app shows your `user_id` and a `pairing_key_hex`. Copy both and feed them into your backend's `client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key=bytes.fromhex(...))` so it can encrypt for you. (V1 dev-mode handoff; V1.5 will wire this automatically via the bootstrap exchange.)
6. Publish your plugin (`client.publish_plugin(...)`) ג€” save the `plugin_row_id`.
7. Run `client.send_to(...)` with a test payload.
8. Within ~15s the phone's inbox poll picks it up, decrypts, fetches your bundle, and renders the card in a WebView.
9. Tap your action button on the phone.
10. Confirm your `/api/action` endpoint received the POST.

## 9. Common errors

- **`401 invalid envelope signature`** ג€” your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** ג€” `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see ֲ§5 vs ֲ§6).
- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** ג€” the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
- **`409 nonce already used`** ג€” your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
- **`429 rate limited`** ג€” back off + retry per `Retry-After` header.
- **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch ג€” missing registerPlugin() call?"** ג€” your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See ֲ§3.
- **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** ג€” your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.
- **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** ג€” caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see ֲ§2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters ג€” emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
- **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** ג€” your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.

Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.

.triad\40-gemini-review.txt:6:*   **Verdict:** If V1.5 (disk persistence) is strictly required for this to work, then Phase 4 is technically "complete" as a data-layer update. .triad\43-codex-review-log.txt:4135:[P2] [EncryptedUserState.kt:55-57](/absent/path/not-used) keeps `deleted_messages` under `SCHEMA_V2`. I would hold for a `SCHEMA_V3` bump if any M11.5/V2 APK can still sync. An older V2 client will parse the blob, ignore `deleted_messages`, and later write back schema 2 without that field, resurrecting deleted messages on M11.6 devices. The existing future-schema push guard only protects you if this field moves to V3.

  17: import kotlinx.coroutines.flow.MutableStateFlow

  28: /**
  29:  * Pulls messages from /v1/messages/inbox on demand, decrypts each one with the
  30:  * matching paired sender's pairing key, and (lazily) downloads the plugin
  31:  * bundle so the inbox UI can render it via a WebView.
  32:  *
  33:  * Bundle cache lives for the process lifetime; on app restart we re-fetch.
  34:  * That's fine for V1 ג€” caching across launches is an M11+ refinement that
  35:  * needs invalidation tied to plugin version updates.
  36:  */
  37: @Singleton
  38: class InboxRepository @Inject constructor(
  39:     private val api: SynclerApi,
  40:     private val session: Session,
  41:     private val pairedSenderStore: PairedSenderStore,
  42: ) {
  43:     private val _items = MutableStateFlow<List<InboxItem>>(emptyList())
  44:     val items: StateFlow<List<InboxItem>> = _items.asStateFlow()
  45: 
  46:     private val bundleHttp = OkHttpClient.Builder()
  47:         // Release builds refuse cleartext outright; debug allows it so devs
  48:         // can host bundles on a LAN box. Matches PluginLoader.requireHttps.
  49:         .connectionSpecs(
  50:             if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
  51:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
  52:             } else {
  53:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
  54:             },
  55:         )
  56:         .build()
  57:     /**
  58:      * Bundle cache keyed by SHA-256 hash (lowercase hex). Multiple plugin
  59:      * versions coexist: a new publish doesn't evict the old version, so old
  60:      * messages keep rendering against the EXACT bundle they were originally
  61:      * validated for (Codex's M11.3 concern: avoid history drift when a
  62:      * plugin author publishes a render-incompatible v2).
  63:      *
  64:      * In-memory only in V1 ג€” survives process lifetime, lost on restart.
  65:      * Disk persistence with size-based eviction is V1.5 (see also
  66:      * `docs/integration-guide.md` ֲ§9 "Common errors" for the user-visible
  67:      * "Plugin couldn't be re-fetched" path).
  68:      */
  69:     private val bundleByHash = mutableMapOf<String, CachedBundle>()
  70:     private val pluginMutex = Mutex()
  71: 
  72:     private var lastSince: String? = null
  73:     private val pollMutex = Mutex()
  74: 
  75:     suspend fun refresh(): Result<Int> = pollMutex.withLock {
  76:         runCatching {
  77:             val response = api.inbox(since = lastSince)
  78:             val userId = session.currentUserId() ?: return@runCatching 0
  79:             val pairings = pairedSenderStore.pairedSenders.value.associateBy { it.senderId }
  80: 
  81:             val newDecrypted = response.messages.mapNotNull { dto ->
  82:                 val sender = pairings[dto.senderId] ?: run {
  83:                     Timber.tag(TAG).w("no paired sender for senderId=%s; skipping", dto.senderId)
  84:                     return@mapNotNull null
  85:                 }
  86:                 if (sender.pairingKey.size != 32) {
  87:                     Timber.tag(TAG).w("paired sender %s has no pairing key; skipping", dto.senderId)
  88:                     return@mapNotNull null
  89:                 }
  90:                 val decrypted = decrypt(dto, userId = userId, pairingKey = sender.pairingKey, senderName = sender.senderName)
  91:                     ?: return@mapNotNull null
  92:                 // Resolve plugin bundle by historical row UUID (NOT by current
  93:                 // /latest) so old messages render against the exact bundle
  94:                 // they were validated for. Codex review 40: a sender publishing
  95:                 // v2 must not retroactively change v1 messages' render output.
  96:                 val plugin = fetchPluginByRowOrNull(dto.pluginId)
  97:                 decrypted.copy(
  98:                     bundleJs = plugin?.bundleJs,
  99:                     declaredEndpoints = plugin?.endpoints.orEmpty(),
 100:                     bundleHash = plugin?.bundleHashHex,
 101:                     revocationReason = plugin?.revocationReason,
 102:                 )
 103:             }
 104: 
 105:             if (newDecrypted.isNotEmpty()) {
 106:                 val merged = (newDecrypted + _items.value).distinctBy { it.id }
 107:                 // Sort by parsed Instant, not by raw string. ISO timestamps
 108:                 // with variable fractional seconds sort lexically the wrong
 109:                 // way ("ג€¦10:00:00Z" > "ג€¦10:00:00.500Z") and would put older
 110:                 // messages above newer ones in the feed. Items that fail to
 111:                 // parse fall to the bottom so a corrupt timestamp can't
 112:                 // hijack the top of the inbox.
 113:                 _items.value = merged.sortedWith(
 114:                     compareByDescending<InboxItem> { parseInstantOrNull(it.sentAt) }
 115:                         .thenByDescending { it.id },
 116:                 )
 117:             }
 118:             response.nextSince?.let { lastSince = it }
 119:             newDecrypted.size
 120:         }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "refresh failed") }
 121:     }
 122: 
 123:     /**
 124:      * Fetches the historical manifest for `pluginRowId` via the by-id
 125:      * endpoint, verifies the bundle, caches bytes BY HASH. The row UUID
 126:      * resolves to the exact bundle that was active when the message was
 127:      * sent ג€” survives later sender publishes AND surfaces revocation
 128:      * state (silent for ``superseded``, alert for ``compromised``, etc.).
 129:      *
 130:      * Already-cached hashes short-circuit. If the row's revocation_reason
 131:      * is ``compromised``, refuse to load the bundle ג€” the render path
 132:      * shows the security warning instead.
 133:      */
 134:     private suspend fun fetchPluginByRowOrNull(pluginRowId: String): CachedBundle? {
 135:         return runCatching {
 136:             val manifest = api.getPluginById(pluginRowId = pluginRowId)
 137: 
 138:             // Hard refusal: compromised plugins MUST NOT execute regardless
 139:             // of cache state. Surface the reason on the InboxItem; the UI
 140:             // shows a security banner instead of the WebView.
 141:             if (manifest.revocationReason == "compromised") {
 142:                 return@runCatching CachedBundle(
 143:                     bundleJs = null,
 144:                     endpoints = emptyList(),
 145:                     bundleHashHex = null,
 146:                     revocationReason = manifest.revocationReason,
 147:                 )
 148:             }
 149: 
 150:             val expectedHashBytes = runCatching { manifest.bundleHash.base64ToBytes() }.getOrNull()
 151:                 ?: error("plugin bundle_hash is not valid base64")
 152:             val expectedHashHex = expectedHashBytes.joinToString("") { "%02x".format(it) }
 153: 
 154:             // Cache hit by hash ג€” same plugin version we already verified.
 155:             pluginMutex.withLock { bundleByHash[expectedHashHex] }?.let { existing ->
 156:                 // Refresh revocation_reason on cache hit so a newly-revoked
 157:                 // plugin gets its banner even if its bytes were cached previously.
 158:                 return@runCatching existing.copy(revocationReason = manifest.revocationReason)
 159:             }
 160: 
 161:             // Scheme check. Release: HTTPS only. Debug: any HTTP for LAN dev.
 162:             val url = manifest.signedBundleUrl
 163:             val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
 164:             if (!schemeOk) error("plugin bundle URL must be HTTPS (got $url)")
 165: 
 166:             val bundleBytes = withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
 167:                 bundleHttp.newCall(Request.Builder().url(url).build()).execute().use { resp ->
 168:                     if (!resp.isSuccessful) error("plugin bundle HTTP ${resp.code}")
 169:                     resp.body?.bytes() ?: error("empty plugin bundle body")
 170:                 }
 171:             }
 172:             // SHA-256(bundle) must equal the server-published bundle_hash.
 173:             val actualHash = MessageDigest.getInstance("SHA-256").digest(bundleBytes)
 174:             if (!actualHash.contentEquals(expectedHashBytes)) {
 175:                 error("plugin bundle hash mismatch (CDN/MITM substitution?)")
 176:             }
 177: 
 178:             val cached = CachedBundle(
 179:                 bundleJs = bundleBytes.toString(Charsets.UTF_8),
 180:                 endpoints = manifest.endpoints,
 181:                 bundleHashHex = expectedHashHex,
 182:                 revocationReason = manifest.revocationReason,
 183:             )
 184:             pluginMutex.withLock { bundleByHash[expectedHashHex] = cached }
 185:             cached
 186:         }.onFailure {
 187:             Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "plugin fetch failed for row %s", pluginRowId)
 188:         }.getOrNull()
 189:     }
 190: 
 191:     /**
 192:      * The cache entry for a verified plugin bundle. `bundleJs` is null when
 193:      * the bundle is refused (compromised revocation); the UI uses
 194:      * `revocationReason` to decide what banner to show in that case.
 195:      */
 196:     data class CachedBundle(
 197:         val bundleJs: String?,
 198:         val endpoints: List<String>,
 199:         val bundleHashHex: String?,
 200:         val revocationReason: String?,
 201:     )
 202: 
 203:     private fun decrypt(
 204:         dto: MessageInboxItemDto,
 205:         userId: String,
 206:         pairingKey: ByteArray,
 207:         senderName: String,
 208:     ): InboxItem? = runCatching {
 209:         val aad = MessageAad(
 210:             senderId = dto.senderId,
 211:             userId = userId,
 212:             pluginId = dto.pluginId,
 213:             // Sender uses empty string when min_plugin_version isn't set; server
 214:             // stores null and returns null over the wire ג€” reconstruct ""
 215:             // so the AAD bytes match what the sender signed/encrypted.
 216:             minPluginVersion = dto.minPluginVersion ?: "",
 217:             expiresAt = dto.expiresAt,
 218:         ).toCanonicalJsonBytes()
 219: 
 220:         val nonce = dto.nonce.base64ToBytes()
 221:         val ciphertext = dto.encryptedBody.base64ToBytes()
 222:         // Aead.decrypt expects (nonce || ciphertext) concatenated; wire splits
 223:         // them, so we reassemble before handing to the AES-GCM primitive.
 224:         val wire = nonce + ciphertext
 225:         val plaintext = Aead.decrypt(pairingKey, wire, aad)
 226: 
 227:         val plaintextString = plaintext.toString(Charsets.UTF_8)
 228:         InboxItem(
 229:             id = dto.id,
 230:             senderId = dto.senderId,
 231:             senderName = senderName,
 232:             pluginId = dto.pluginId,
 233:             pluginIdentifier = dto.pluginIdentifier,
 234:             payloadJson = plaintextString,
 235:             sentAt = dto.sentAt,
 236:             expiresAt = dto.expiresAt,
 237:             bundleJs = null,
 238:             declaredEndpoints = emptyList(),
 239:             bundleHash = null,
 240:             revocationReason = null,
 241:             hostPreview = HostPreviewParser.parse(plaintextString),
 242:         )
 243:     }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "decrypt failed for message %s", dto.id) }.getOrNull()
 244: 
 245:     private fun parseInstantOrNull(s: String): Instant? =
 246:         runCatching { Instant.parse(s) }.getOrNull()
 247: 
 248:     companion object {
 249:         const val TAG = "InboxRepo"
 250: 
 251:         /**
 252:          * Groups inbox items by senderId and sorts the groups by most-recent
 253:          * activity. Within each group, items are already sorted newest-first
 254:          * (the [InboxRepository.refresh] sort).
 255:          */
 256:         fun groupItemsBySender(items: List<InboxItem>): List<Pair<String, List<InboxItem>>> {
 257:             return items.groupBy { it.senderId }
 258:                 .toList()
 259:                 .sortedByDescending { (_, list) ->
 260:                     list.maxOfOrNull { runCatching { Instant.parse(it.sentAt) }.getOrNull()?.toEpochMilli() ?: 0L } ?: 0L
 261:                 }
 262:         }
 263:     }
 264: }

 266: data class InboxItem(
 267:     val id: String,
 268:     val senderId: String,
 269:     val senderName: String,
 270:     val pluginId: String,
 271:     val pluginIdentifier: String,
 272:     val payloadJson: String,
 273:     val sentAt: String,
 274:     val expiresAt: String,
 275:     /**
 276:      * Plugin JS bundle source. Null when the fetch is in-flight or failed ג€”
 277:      * the UI surfaces a fallback error card in that case (still pullable from
 278:      * the inbox; detail view can retry).
 279:      */
 280:     val bundleJs: String?,
 281:     /**
 282:      * Endpoints the plugin's manifest declared (glob patterns like
 283:      * `https://lottery.app/api/...`). The card's network bridge refuses
 284:      * `platform.network.fetch` calls to URLs that don't match any pattern.
 285:      */
 286:     val declaredEndpoints: List<String>,
 287:     /**
 288:      * SHA-256 (lowercase hex) of the bundle this message was originally
 289:      * validated against (M11.4). Null until a successful fetch. The render
 290:      * path uses this hash to look up the cached bundle, so old messages keep
 291:      * rendering against the bundle they were verified for even after the
 292:      * plugin author publishes a render-incompatible new version.
 293:      */
 294:     val bundleHash: String?,
 295:     /**
 296:      * Revocation classification when the plugin row this message references
 297:      * has been pulled. One of: ``superseded`` (silent ג€” UX may show subdued
 298:      * banner), ``compromised`` (refuse to render; show security warning),
 299:      * ``sender_disabled`` (render with "no longer available" banner),
 300:      * ``unspecified`` (pre-M11.4 legacy revoke ג€” treat conservatively).
 301:      * Null on active rows.
 302:      */
 303:     val revocationReason: String?,
 304:     /**
 305:      * Structured row metadata extracted from the decrypted payload's reserved
 306:      * `hostPreview` key. Null when the sender didn't supply one or the block
 307:      * was malformed (logged and ignored ג€” the row falls back to a generic
 308:      * "New message from {senderName}" rendering).
 309:      */
 310:     val hostPreview: HostPreview?,
 311: )
 312: 
 313: /**
 314:  * Mirror of sdk-plugin/HostPreview. Senders embed this under the reserved
 315:  * `hostPreview` key of the encrypted payload; the host parses it post-decrypt
 316:  * to render the inbox row natively without invoking the plugin's `render()`.
 317:  *
 318:  * `searchText` is folded into the host's global search index in addition to
 319:  * the visible fields. The plugin's `render(payload)` (detail view) still
 320:  * receives the entire decrypted payload, including the hostPreview block.
 321:  */
 322: data class HostPreview(
 323:     val title: String,
 324:     val subtitle: String?,
 325:     val summary: String?,
 326:     val searchText: List<String>,
 327: )

   1: package app.syncler.core.storage
   2: 
   3: import org.json.JSONArray
   4: import org.json.JSONObject
   5: 
   6: /**
   7:  * Structured user state ג€” what the encrypted blob deserializes to after
   8:  * the client decrypts it with the master key.
   9:  *
  10:  * Schema version is embedded so future migrations can detect old blobs
  11:  * and run a one-shot migration step before merging.
  12:  */
  13: data class EncryptedUserState(
  14:     val schemaVersion: Int = SCHEMA_CURRENT,
  15:     val installedPlugins: List<InstalledPluginRef> = emptyList(),
  16:     val dismissedMessages: List<DismissedMessageEntry> = emptyList(),
  17:     val pluginSettings: Map<String, PluginSettings> = emptyMap(),
  18:     /** Per-plugin user-scoped storage (I1 storage scope = "user"). */
  19:     val userScopedStorage: Map<String, Map<String, String>> = emptyMap(),
  20:     /** M11.2: per-message read state, synced across user's devices. */
  21:     val readMessages: List<ReadMessageEntry> = emptyList(),
  22:     /** M11.2: per-message archive state, distinct from dismissal. */
  23:     val archivedMessages: List<ArchivedMessageEntry> = emptyList(),
  24:     /** M11.6: per-message delete state. Hidden from all surfaces; merges as union. */
  25:     val deletedMessages: List<DeletedMessageEntry> = emptyList(),
  26: ) {
  27:     fun toJson(): String = JSONObject().apply {
  28:         put("schema_version", schemaVersion)
  29:         put("installed_plugins", JSONArray().apply {
  30:             installedPlugins.forEach { put(it.toJson()) }
  31:         })
  32:         put("dismissed_messages", JSONArray().apply {
  33:             dismissedMessages.forEach { put(it.toJson()) }
  34:         })
  35:         put("plugin_settings", JSONObject().apply {
  36:             pluginSettings.forEach { (k, v) -> put(k, v.toJson()) }
  37:         })
  38:         put("user_scoped_storage", JSONObject().apply {
  39:             userScopedStorage.forEach { (pluginId, kvs) ->
  40:                 put(pluginId, JSONObject().apply { kvs.forEach { (k, v) -> put(k, v) } })
  41:             }
  42:         })
  43:         put("read_messages", JSONArray().apply {
  44:             readMessages.forEach { put(it.toJson()) }
  45:         })
  46:         put("archived_messages", JSONArray().apply {
  47:             archivedMessages.forEach { put(it.toJson()) }
  48:         })
  49:         put("deleted_messages", JSONArray().apply {
  50:             deletedMessages.forEach { put(it.toJson()) }
  51:         })
  52:     }.toString()
  53: 
  54:     companion object {
  55:         const val SCHEMA_V1 = 1
  56:         const val SCHEMA_V2 = 2
  57:         const val SCHEMA_V3 = 3
  58:         const val SCHEMA_CURRENT = SCHEMA_V3
  59: 
  60:         /** Pre-V1 blobs (no schema_version field) ג€” migrated forward at parse. */
  61:         const val SCHEMA_V0 = 0
  62: 
  63:         fun fromJson(json: String): EncryptedUserState {
  64:             if (json.isEmpty()) return EncryptedUserState()
  65:             val obj = JSONObject(json)
  66:             // Absent schema_version = V0 (pre-V1). We treat it explicitly
  67:             // rather than silently calling it V1, so future migrations can
  68:             // route the blob through a dedicated upgrade step.
  69:             val schema = if (obj.has("schema_version")) obj.getInt("schema_version") else SCHEMA_V0
  70:             return EncryptedUserState(
  71:                 schemaVersion = when (schema) {
  72:                     SCHEMA_V0, SCHEMA_V1, SCHEMA_V2 -> SCHEMA_CURRENT  // forward-migrate
  73:                     else -> schema
  74:                 },
  75:                 installedPlugins = obj.optJSONArray("installed_plugins")
  76:                     ?.let { arr ->
  77:                         (0 until arr.length()).mapNotNull {
  78:                             runCatching { InstalledPluginRef.fromJson(arr.getJSONObject(it)) }.getOrNull()
  79:                         }
  80:                     }
  81:                     .orEmpty(),
  82:                 dismissedMessages = obj.optJSONArray("dismissed_messages")
  83:                     ?.let { arr ->
  84:                         (0 until arr.length()).mapNotNull {
  85:                             runCatching { DismissedMessageEntry.fromJson(arr.getJSONObject(it)) }.getOrNull()
  86:                         }
  87:                     }
  88:                     .orEmpty(),
  89:                 pluginSettings = obj.optJSONObject("plugin_settings")
  90:                     ?.let { o ->
  91:                         o.keys().asSequence().mapNotNull { key ->
  92:                             runCatching { key to PluginSettings.fromJson(o.getJSONObject(key)) }.getOrNull()
  93:                         }.toMap()
  94:                     }
  95:                     .orEmpty(),
  96:                 userScopedStorage = obj.optJSONObject("user_scoped_storage")
  97:                     ?.let { o ->
  98:                         o.keys().asSequence().mapNotNull { pluginId ->
  99:                             runCatching {
 100:                                 val nested = o.getJSONObject(pluginId)
 101:                                 pluginId to nested.keys().asSequence().mapNotNull { k ->
 102:                                     runCatching { k to nested.getString(k) }.getOrNull()
 103:                                 }.toMap()
 104:                             }.getOrNull()
 105:                         }.toMap()
 106:                     }
 107:                     .orEmpty(),
 108:                 // V1 blobs lack these fields ג€” fromJson returns empty lists,
 109:                 // which is the correct semantics (no messages read/archived
 110:                 // yet from the V1 device's perspective).
 111:                 readMessages = obj.optJSONArray("read_messages")
 112:                     ?.let { arr ->
 113:                         (0 until arr.length()).mapNotNull {
 114:                             runCatching { ReadMessageEntry.fromJson(arr.getJSONObject(it)) }.getOrNull()
 115:                         }
 116:                     }
 117:                     .orEmpty(),
 118:                 archivedMessages = obj.optJSONArray("archived_messages")
 119:                     ?.let { arr ->
 120:                         (0 until arr.length()).mapNotNull {
 121:                             runCatching { ArchivedMessageEntry.fromJson(arr.getJSONObject(it)) }.getOrNull()
 122:                         }
 123:                     }
 124:                     .orEmpty(),
 125:                 deletedMessages = obj.optJSONArray("deleted_messages")
 126:                     ?.let { arr ->
 127:                         (0 until arr.length()).mapNotNull {
 128:                             runCatching { DeletedMessageEntry.fromJson(arr.getJSONObject(it)) }.getOrNull()
 129:                         }
 130:                     }
 131:                     .orEmpty(),
 132:             )
 133:         }
 134:     }
 135: }

 138:     val pluginId: String,

 155:             installedAt = o.getString("installed_at"),

 160: data class DismissedMessageEntry(
 161:     val messageId: String,
 162:     val dismissedAt: String,
 163: ) {
 164:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 165:         put("message_id", messageId)
 166:         put("dismissed_at", dismissedAt)
 167:     }
 168: 
 169:     companion object {
 170:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = DismissedMessageEntry(
 171:             messageId = o.getString("message_id"),
 172:             dismissedAt = o.getString("dismissed_at"),
 173:         )
 174:     }
 175: }
 176: 
 177: /**
 178:  * M11.2: a message the user has marked read on at least one device. Synced
 179:  * via the M7 CAS state blob. Merge resolves conflicts by max(readAt) per
 180:  * messageId ג€” i.e. the most recently-set read timestamp wins, which works
 181:  * because "read" is a monotone state (you don't go from read to unread
 182:  * silently; a manual "mark unread" would be a separate action that writes a
 183:  * tombstone, not in V1).
 184:  */
 185: data class ReadMessageEntry(
 186:     val messageId: String,
 187:     val readAt: String,
 188: ) {
 189:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 190:         put("message_id", messageId)
 191:         put("read_at", readAt)
 192:     }
 193: 
 194:     companion object {
 195:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = ReadMessageEntry(
 196:             messageId = o.getString("message_id"),
 197:             readAt = o.getString("read_at"),
 198:         )
 199:     }
 200: }
 201: 
 202: /**
 203:  * M11.2: a message the user has archived. The archive state is synced via
 204:  * the M7 CAS blob so an archive on one device shows up across all of the
 205:  * user's devices.
 206:  *
 207:  * V1 semantic limit (called out in review 39 by Codex): "archived" is a
 208:  * *filter* over the still-fetchable inbox ג€” we don't persist the message
 209:  * body locally beyond the server's 30-day retention cap. Once the server
 210:  * expires the message, the archived id remains in this list but there's
 211:  * no body to render. A proper "keep past expiry" archive needs a local
 212:  * message body store and is V1.5 work. For now, treat archive as
 213:  * "hide from the active inbox while the server still has the message."
 214:  *
 215:  * Distinct from "dismiss": dismiss is a server-side message lifecycle
 216:  * action (POST /v1/messages/.../dismiss). Archive is purely the user's
 217:  * cross-device organization state.
 218:  */
 219: data class ArchivedMessageEntry(
 220:     val messageId: String,
 221:     val archivedAt: String,
 222: ) {
 223:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 224:         put("message_id", messageId)
 225:         put("archived_at", archivedAt)
 226:     }
 227: 
 228:     companion object {
 229:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = ArchivedMessageEntry(
 230:             messageId = o.getString("message_id"),
 231:             archivedAt = o.getString("archived_at"),
 232:         )
 233:     }
 234: }
 235: 
 236: /**
 237:  * M11.6: per-message deletion. Distinct from archive: deleted messages are
 238:  * hidden from BOTH the inbox AND the archive screen ג€” the user said "make
 239:  * it go away." Synced via the M7 CAS blob so deleting on one device hides
 240:  * the card everywhere. Like archive, this is local state only; the server
 241:  * still has the message until its retention cap expires.
 242:  *
 243:  * Merge semantics: union by message_id, max(deleted_at) wins on conflict.
 244:  * No undelete in V1 ג€” the entry is monotone.
 245:  */
 246: data class DeletedMessageEntry(
 247:     val messageId: String,
 248:     val deletedAt: String,
 249: ) {
 250:     fun toJson(): JSONObject = JSONObject().apply {
 251:         put("message_id", messageId)
 252:         put("deleted_at", deletedAt)
 253:     }
 254: 
 255:     companion object {
 256:         fun fromJson(o: JSONObject) = DeletedMessageEntry(
 257:             messageId = o.getString("message_id"),
 258:             deletedAt = o.getString("deleted_at"),
 259:         )
 260:     }

 526: /**
 527:  * Case-insensitive substring match across visible row fields plus the
 528:  * `hostPreview.searchText` tokens the sender pre-indexed. Plugin author
 529:  * promised in ֲ§2 of the integration guide that searchText would be
 530:  * folded into host search ג€” this is where that promise gets paid.
 531:  */
 532: internal fun matchesQuery(item: InboxItem, rawQuery: String): Boolean {
 533:     val q = rawQuery.trim().lowercase(Locale.ROOT)
 534:     if (q.isEmpty()) return true
 535:     if (item.senderName.lowercase(Locale.ROOT).contains(q)) return true
 536:     item.hostPreview?.let { preview ->
 537:         if (preview.title.lowercase(Locale.ROOT).contains(q)) return true
 538:         if (preview.subtitle?.lowercase(Locale.ROOT)?.contains(q) == true) return true
 539:         if (preview.summary?.lowercase(Locale.ROOT)?.contains(q) == true) return true
 540:         if (preview.searchText.any { it.lowercase(Locale.ROOT).contains(q) }) return true
 541:     }
 542:     return false
 543: }

 545: /**
 546:  * Groups inbox items into Today / Yesterday / Earlier buckets and renders
 547:  * them with sticky-ish section headers. Bucket boundaries are computed
 548:  * against the device's current local date (the row timestamp is the server's
 549:  * `sent_at`, which is UTC; we convert per-row to local for bucketing).
 550:  */
 551: @Composable
 552: private fun BucketedInboxList(
 553:     items: List<InboxItem>,
 554:     readMessageIds: Set<String>,
 555:     selectedIds: Set<String>,
 556:     onItemClick: (String) -> Unit,
 557:     onItemLongClick: (String) -> Unit,
 558: ) {
 559:     val today = LocalDate.now()
 560:     val buckets = remember(items, today) {
 561:         items.groupBy { item ->
 562:             bucketFor(item.sentAt, today)
 563:         }.toSortedMap(compareBy { it.order })
 564:     }
 565:     LazyColumn(verticalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(8.dp)) {
 566:         buckets.forEach { (bucket, bucketItems) ->
 567:             item(key = "header-${bucket.name}") {
 568:                 Text(
 569:                     text = bucket.label,
 570:                     style = MaterialTheme.typography.titleSmall,
 571:                     color = MaterialTheme.colorScheme.onSurfaceVariant,
 572:                     modifier = Modifier.padding(top = 12.dp, bottom = 4.dp),
 573:                 )
 574:             }
 575:             items(bucketItems, key = { it.id }) { item ->
 576:                 InboxRow(
 577:                     item = item,
 578:                     isRead = item.id in readMessageIds,
 579:                     isSelected = item.id in selectedIds,
 580:                     onClick = { onItemClick(item.id) },
 581:                     onLongClick = { onItemLongClick(item.id) },
 582:                 )
 583:             }
 584:         }
 585:     }
 586: }

  38: /**
  39:  * Owns the user's [EncryptedUserState] across the app lifecycle.
  40:  *
  41:  *  - **Local-first:** writes go to disk immediately (encrypted at rest via
  42:  *    EncryptedSharedPreferences); UI reactions don't wait for the network.
  43:  *  - **M7 CAS sync:** [pull] fetches the server blob, decrypts with the
  44:  *    user's master key, merges with local via [StateMerger], persists, and
  45:  *    rewrites the local state. [push] encrypts the local state, PUTs to
  46:  *    `/v1/state` with the last-known version, and on 409 conflict pulls
  47:  *    the freshest blob, re-merges, and retries once.
  48:  *  - **Master-key dependence:** sync no-ops when the session is locked
  49:  *    (no master key in memory). Local writes still proceed ג€” the app
  50:  *    works offline; pushes happen when the user next unlocks.
  51:  *
  52:  * Read state is the V1 primary use case. Archived state is wired through
  53:  * the same channel for Phase 3.
  54:  */
  55: @Singleton
  56: class UserStateRepository @Inject constructor(
  57:     @ApplicationContext context: Context,
  58:     private val api: SynclerApi,
  59:     private val session: Session,
  60: ) {
  61:     // Not injected: the @Singleton has no Hilt provider for Clock. Tests use
  62:     // the secondary constructor below to inject a fake.
  63:     private val clock: Clock = Clock.systemUTC()
  64:     private val scope = CoroutineScope(SupervisorJob() + Dispatchers.IO)
  65: 
  66:     init {
  67:         // Auto-clear local state when the session locks (logout, JWT expiry,
  68:         // process restart without password). Without this, a subsequent
  69:         // login on the same device would inherit the previous user's read
  70:         // marks AND push them up to the new user's server account.
  71:         //
  72:         // We drop(1) so the initial Locked-at-startup emission (before any
  73:         // login) doesn't trigger a redundant clear of the disk state we
  74:         // just loaded ג€” clear only runs on a *transition* away from
  75:         // unlocked.
  76:         session.sessionState
  77:             .map { it.isUnlocked }
  78:             .distinctUntilChanged()
  79:             .drop(1)
  80:             .onEach { unlocked -> if (!unlocked) clearInternal() }
  81:             .launchIn(scope)
  82:     }
  83:     private val prefs: SharedPreferences = EncryptedSharedPreferences.create(
  84:         context,
  85:         PREFS_NAME,
  86:         MasterKey.Builder(context).setKeyScheme(MasterKey.KeyScheme.AES256_GCM).build(),
  87:         EncryptedSharedPreferences.PrefKeyEncryptionScheme.AES256_SIV,
  88:         EncryptedSharedPreferences.PrefValueEncryptionScheme.AES256_GCM,
  89:     )
  90: 
  91:     private val _state = MutableStateFlow(loadFromDisk())
  92:     val state: StateFlow<EncryptedUserState> = _state.asStateFlow()
  93: 
  94:     private val syncMutex = Mutex()
  95: 
  96:     /**
  97:      * Marks the message as read locally (immediate) and schedules a push.
  98:      * Idempotent ג€” re-marking an already-read message refreshes the
  99:      * timestamp, which is harmless and lets future "most-recent device"
 100:      * conflict resolution pick the right winner.
 101:      *
 102:      * The local mutation is atomic via [MutableStateFlow.update]: two
 103:      * concurrent calls cannot lose each other's entries. The disk write
 104:      * happens inside the same critical section as the in-memory update so
 105:      * a process kill mid-write doesn't expose an inconsistent state.
 106:      */
 107:     suspend fun markRead(messageId: String) {
 108:         val now = Instant.now(clock).toString()
 109:         mutateLocal { current ->
 110:             val others = current.readMessages.filterNot { it.messageId == messageId }
 111:             current.copy(readMessages = others + ReadMessageEntry(messageId, now))
 112:         }
 113:         markDirtyAndPush()
 114:     }
 115: 
 116:     /** Archives a message locally; pushes asynchronously. */
 117:     suspend fun markArchived(messageId: String) {
 118:         val now = Instant.now(clock).toString()
 119:         mutateLocal { current ->
 120:             val others = current.archivedMessages.filterNot { it.messageId == messageId }
 121:             current.copy(archivedMessages = others + ArchivedMessageEntry(messageId, now))
 122:         }
 123:         markDirtyAndPush()
 124:     }
 125: 
 126:     /** Bulk archive for multi-select. Single mutation + single push. */
 127:     suspend fun markManyArchived(messageIds: Collection<String>) {
 128:         if (messageIds.isEmpty()) return
 129:         val now = Instant.now(clock).toString()
 130:         val ids = messageIds.toSet()
 131:         mutateLocal { current ->
 132:             val keep = current.archivedMessages.filterNot { it.messageId in ids }
 133:             val newEntries = ids.map { ArchivedMessageEntry(it, now) }
 134:             current.copy(archivedMessages = keep + newEntries)
 135:         }
 136:         markDirtyAndPush()
 137:     }
 138: 
 139:     /**
 140:      * Removes the message from the archive set, returning it to the active
 141:      * inbox. Note: this is a local "forget the archive mark" operation, not
 142:      * a tombstone ג€” if another device has a still-current archive entry for
 143:      * the same message and we re-pull before pushing, the merge's
 144:      * max(archivedAt)-wins rule will resurrect the archive locally. V1
 145:      * accepts that tiny race in exchange for not encoding tombstones
 146:      * (which would need a separate tombstones list and explicit GC).
 147:      */
 148:     suspend fun markUnarchived(messageId: String) {
 149:         mutateLocal { current ->
 150:             current.copy(
 151:                 archivedMessages = current.archivedMessages.filterNot { it.messageId == messageId },
 152:             )
 153:         }
 154:         markDirtyAndPush()
 155:     }
 156: 
 157:     /**
 158:      * M11.6: marks a message deleted. Distinct from archive ג€” deleted
 159:      * messages are hidden from BOTH the inbox and the archive screen.
 160:      * Merge semantics are monotone (no undelete in V1) so this entry
 161:      * permanently wins across devices.
 162:      */
 163:     suspend fun markDeleted(messageId: String) {
 164:         val now = Instant.now(clock).toString()
 165:         mutateLocal { current ->
 166:             val others = current.deletedMessages.filterNot { it.messageId == messageId }
 167:             current.copy(deletedMessages = others + DeletedMessageEntry(messageId, now))
 168:         }
 169:         markDirtyAndPush()
 170:     }
 171: 
 172:     suspend fun markManyDeleted(messageIds: Collection<String>) {
 173:         if (messageIds.isEmpty()) return
 174:         val now = Instant.now(clock).toString()
 175:         val ids = messageIds.toSet()
 176:         mutateLocal { current ->
 177:             val keep = current.deletedMessages.filterNot { it.messageId in ids }
 178:             val newEntries = ids.map { DeletedMessageEntry(it, now) }
 179:             current.copy(deletedMessages = keep + newEntries)
 180:         }
 181:         markDirtyAndPush()
 182:     }
 183: 
 184:     /**
 185:      * Atomic local-state mutation. Holds [syncMutex] so a concurrent [pull]
 186:      * cannot interleave its merge between the read and the write here, and
 187:      * so disk persistence is also serialized.
 188:      */
 189:     private suspend fun mutateLocal(transform: (EncryptedUserState) -> EncryptedUserState) {
 190:         syncMutex.withLock {
 191:             val next = transform(_state.value)
 192:             _state.value = next
 193:             persist(next)
 194:         }
 195:     }
 196: 
 197:     private fun markDirty() {
 198:         prefs.edit().putBoolean(KEY_DIRTY, true).apply()
 199:     }
 200: 
 201:     private fun clearDirty() {
 202:         prefs.edit().putBoolean(KEY_DIRTY, false).apply()
 203:     }
 204: 
 205:     private fun isDirty(): Boolean = prefs.getBoolean(KEY_DIRTY, false)
 206: 
 207:     private suspend fun markDirtyAndPush() {
 208:         markDirty()
 209:         runCatching { push() }.onFailure {
 210:             // Local change still on disk + flagged dirty; flushPendingPush on
 211:             // next foreground/refresh will retry.
 212:             Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "push failed; flagged dirty for retry")
 213:         }
 214:     }
 215: 
 216:     /**
 217:      * Attempts to push the local state if dirty. Called by [InboxViewModel]
 218:      * on init and on refresh, so a push that 409'd or hit network failure
 219:      * gets retried without requiring another user action.
 220:      */
 221:     suspend fun flushPendingPush(): Result<Unit> {
 222:         if (!isDirty()) return Result.success(Unit)
 223:         return push()
 224:     }
 225: 
 226:     /**
 227:      * Fetches the remote state, merges with local, persists. Safe to call
 228:      * on app foreground / inbox refresh. No-op when the session is locked.
 229:      *
 230:      * The entire fetch-merge-persist runs inside [syncMutex] so concurrent
 231:      * [markRead] / [markArchived] cannot interleave between the merge
 232:      * computation and the disk write.
 233:      */
 234:     suspend fun pull(): Result<Unit> = syncMutex.withLock {
 235:         val masterKey = session.sessionState.value.masterKey ?: return@withLock Result.success(Unit)
 236:         runCatching {
 237:             val response = api.getUserState()
 238:             val remoteState = decodeRemote(response.encryptedBlob, masterKey)
 239:             val merged = StateMerger.merge(local = _state.value, remote = remoteState)
 240:             _state.value = merged
 241:             persist(merged, remoteVersion = response.stateVersion)
 242:         }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "pull failed") }
 243:     }
 244: 
 245:     /**
 246:      * Encrypts the local state and PUTs to the server with the last-known
 247:      * CAS version. On 409 conflict: pull-merge-retry once. No-op when the
 248:      * session is locked. Successful push clears the dirty flag.
 249:      */
 250:     suspend fun push(): Result<Unit> = syncMutex.withLock {
 251:         val masterKey = session.sessionState.value.masterKey ?: return@withLock Result.success(Unit)
 252:         // Defensive: a future-schema blob (downloaded by a newer client and
 253:         // somehow persisted on this older one) should NOT be pushed back ג€”
 254:         // we'd write known fields under the future schema_version, losing
 255:         // the V3+ fields the newer client wrote. Refuse-to-push surfaces the
 256:         // version skew as a push failure rather than corrupting state.
 257:         if (_state.value.schemaVersion > EncryptedUserState.SCHEMA_CURRENT) {
 258:             Timber.tag(TAG).w(
 259:                 "refusing to push schema_version %d (client supports %d)",
 260:                 _state.value.schemaVersion, EncryptedUserState.SCHEMA_CURRENT,

 succeeded in 329ms:
 170:             // dirty local change that hasn't been pushed yet.
 171:             userState.pull()
 172:             userState.flushPendingPush()
 173:             _refreshing.value = false
 174:         }
 175:     }
 176: 
 177:     fun open(itemId: String) {
 178:         _selectedId.value = itemId
 179:         // Mark-read trigger: opening the detail view (the conservative trigger
 180:         // both Codex and Gemini argued for in review 35 ג€” scanning the list
 181:         // alone should not punish unread state).
 182:         viewModelScope.launch { userState.markRead(itemId) }
 183:     }
 184:     fun closeDetail() { _selectedId.value = null }
 185: 
 186:     val archivedMessageIds: StateFlow<Set<String>> = userState.state
 187:         .map { st -> st.archivedMessages.map { it.messageId }.toSet() }
 188:         .stateIn(
 189:             scope = viewModelScope,
 190:             started = SharingStarted.WhileSubscribed(5_000),
 191:             initialValue = userState.state.value.archivedMessages.map { it.messageId }.toSet(),
 192:         )
 193: 
 194:     val deletedMessageIds: StateFlow<Set<String>> = userState.state
 195:         .map { st -> st.deletedMessages.map { it.messageId }.toSet() }
 196:         .stateIn(
 197:             scope = viewModelScope,
 198:             started = SharingStarted.WhileSubscribed(5_000),
 199:             initialValue = userState.state.value.deletedMessages.map { it.messageId }.toSet(),
 200:         )
 201: 
 202:     fun archive(itemId: String) {
 203:         viewModelScope.launch { userState.markArchived(itemId) }
 204:     }
 205: 
 206:     fun unarchive(itemId: String) {
 207:         viewModelScope.launch { userState.markUnarchived(itemId) }
 208:     }
 209: 
 210:     fun delete(itemId: String) {
 211:         viewModelScope.launch { userState.markDeleted(itemId) }
 212:     }
 213: 
 214:     private val _showArchive = MutableStateFlow(false)
 215:     val showArchive: StateFlow<Boolean> = _showArchive.asStateFlow()
 216:     fun openArchive() { _showArchive.value = true }
 217:     fun closeArchive() { _showArchive.value = false }
 218: 
 219:     // ---------- M11.7: multi-select ----------
 220:     /**
 221:      * Selection mode is entered by long-pressing a row. While active, rows
 222:      * toggle on tap (instead of opening detail), the top-app-bar swaps to
 223:      * a selection bar with bulk actions, and back exits selection without
 224:      * navigating away.
 225:      */
 226:     private val _selectedIds = MutableStateFlow<Set<String>>(emptySet())
 227:     val selectedIds: StateFlow<Set<String>> = _selectedIds.asStateFlow()
 228:     val selectionMode: StateFlow<Boolean> = _selectedIds
 229:         .map { it.isNotEmpty() }

 661: private enum class DateBucket(val order: Int, val label: String) {
 662:     Today(0, "Today"),
 663:     Yesterday(1, "Yesterday"),
 664:     Earlier(2, "Earlier"),
 665: }
 666: 
 667: private fun bucketFor(isoSentAt: String, today: LocalDate): DateBucket {
 668:     // sent_at is server-canonical UTC; project to the device's local date
 669:     // for bucketing so "Today" matches what the user sees on their clock.
 670:     val date = runCatching {
 671:         Instant.parse(isoSentAt).atZone(ZoneId.systemDefault()).toLocalDate()
 672:     }.getOrNull() ?: return DateBucket.Earlier
 673:     return when {
 674:         date == today -> DateBucket.Today
 675:         date == today.minusDays(1) -> DateBucket.Yesterday
 676:         else -> DateBucket.Earlier
 677:     }
 678: }

  44: def _b64(value: bytes) -> str:
  45:     return base64.b64encode(value).decode("ascii")

  48: def _publish_envelope(payload: PluginPublishRequest) -> bytes:
  49:     envelope = {
  50:         "sender_id": str(payload.sender_id),
  51:         "plugin_identifier": payload.plugin_identifier,
  52:         "version": payload.version,
  53:         "manifest_hash": payload.manifest_hash,
  54:         "bundle_hash": payload.bundle_hash,
  55:         "signature": payload.signature,
  56:         "signed_bundle_url": payload.signed_bundle_url,
  57:         "capabilities": payload.capabilities,
  58:         "endpoints": payload.endpoints,
  59:     }
  60:     return json.dumps(envelope, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")
  61: 
  62: 
  63: def _revoke_envelope(payload: PluginRevokeRequest) -> bytes:
  64:     # Canonical 3-field envelope. Reason is part of the signed bytes so a
  65:     # man-in-the-middle can't strip a "compromised" reason down to a silent
  66:     # "superseded". Backwards compat with M8.1 clients: when reason is None
  67:     # we omit it from the envelope so the signature shape matches.
  68:     envelope: dict[str, str] = {
  69:         "sender_id": str(payload.sender_id),
  70:         "plugin_row_id": str(payload.plugin_row_id),
  71:     }
  72:     if payload.reason is not None:
  73:         envelope["reason"] = payload.reason
  74:     return json.dumps(envelope, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":")).encode("utf-8")
  75:

  77: @router.post("/publish", response_model=PluginPublishResponse, status_code=status.HTTP_201_CREATED)
  78: async def publish(
  79:     payload: PluginPublishRequest,
  80:     request: Request,
  81:     # Pre-auth IP bucket ג€” cheap, prevents body-parsing DoS from anonymous
  82:     # callers. The per-sender bucket is applied below, after sig verification.
  83:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),
  84:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
  85: ) -> PluginPublishResponse:
  86:     try:
  87:         sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
  88:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
  89:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="sender not found") from exc
  90:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
  91:         raise HTTPException(status_code=410, detail="sender revoked") from exc
  92: 
  93:     sender_sig = decode_base64(payload.sender_signature, field_name="sender_signature", exact=64)
  94:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, _publish_envelope(payload), sender_sig):
  95:         raise HTTPException(status_code=401, detail="invalid sender signature")
  96: 
  97:     # Per-sender bucket AFTER signature verification ג€” a spoofer cannot inflate
  98:     # someone else's bucket by setting a foreign sender_id in the body, because
  99:     # they cannot forge the matching Ed25519 signature.
 100:     request.state.sender_id = str(payload.sender_id)
 101:     await check_rate_limit(db, request, RATE_LIMITS["plugin_publish"])
 102: 
 103:     try:
 104:         plugin = await publish_plugin(
 105:             db,
 106:             sender_id=sender.id,
 107:             plugin_identifier=payload.plugin_identifier,
 108:             version=payload.version,
 109:             manifest_hash=decode_base64(payload.manifest_hash, field_name="manifest_hash", exact=32),
 110:             bundle_hash=decode_base64(payload.bundle_hash, field_name="bundle_hash", exact=32),
 111:             signature=decode_base64(payload.signature, field_name="signature", exact=64),
 112:             signed_bundle_url=payload.signed_bundle_url,
 113:             capabilities=payload.capabilities,
 114:             endpoints=payload.endpoints,
 115:         )
 116:     except InvalidVersionError as exc:
 117:         raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 118:     except VersionRegressionError as exc:
 119:         raise HTTPException(status_code=409, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 120:     except DuplicateVersionError as exc:
 121:         raise HTTPException(status_code=409, detail=str(exc)) from exc
 122: 
 123:     return PluginPublishResponse(
 124:         plugin_row_id=plugin.id,
 125:         plugin_identifier=plugin.plugin_identifier,
 126:         version=plugin.version,
 127:         created_at=plugin.created_at,
 128:     )

 165: @router.get("/by-id/{plugin_row_id}", response_model=PluginLatestResponse)
 166: async def by_id(
 167:     plugin_row_id: uuid.UUID,
 168:     # IP-based bucket: /by-id is unauthenticated and has no sender_id in
 169:     # the path for the per-sender bucket to key off. message_send_ip is
 170:     # the cheap pre-auth bucket we use for the same shape elsewhere.
 171:     _: None = Depends(rate_limit("message_send_ip")),
 172:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 173: ) -> PluginLatestResponse:
 174:     """Resolve a plugin manifest by its exact row UUID.
 175: 
 176:     Devices use this for historical lookups (an inbox message carries the
 177:     plugin_row_id it was originally validated against; resolving by row
 178:     UUID guarantees the device renders against the EXACT bundle that was
 179:     in effect at message-send time, even after the sender publishes a
 180:     newer or revoked version under the same plugin_identifier).
 181: 
 182:     Unlike `/latest`, this endpoint returns revoked rows too ג€” with
 183:     `revoked_at` and `revocation_reason` populated so the device can
 184:     apply differentiated UX (refuse-to-execute for `compromised`,
 185:     neutral fallback for `sender_disabled`, etc.).
 186:     """
 187:     try:
 188:         plugin = await get_plugin_by_id(db, plugin_row_id=plugin_row_id)
 189:     except PluginNotFoundError as exc:
 190:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found") from exc
 191: 
 192:     return PluginLatestResponse(
 193:         plugin_row_id=plugin.id,
 194:         sender_id=plugin.sender_id,
 195:         plugin_identifier=plugin.plugin_identifier,
 196:         version=plugin.version,
 197:         signed_bundle_url=plugin.signed_bundle_url,
 198:         manifest_hash=_b64(plugin.manifest_hash),
 199:         bundle_hash=_b64(plugin.bundle_hash),
 200:         signature=_b64(plugin.signature),
 201:         capabilities=plugin.capabilities,
 202:         endpoints=plugin.endpoints,
 203:         created_at=plugin.created_at,
 204:         revoked_at=plugin.revoked_at,
 205:         revocation_reason=plugin.revocation_reason,
 206:     )

 209: @router.post("/revoke", status_code=status.HTTP_204_NO_CONTENT)
 210: async def revoke(
 211:     payload: PluginRevokeRequest,
 212:     db: AsyncSession = Depends(get_db),
 213: ) -> Response:
 214:     """Sender-authenticated plugin row revoke.
 215: 
 216:     M8.1 fix: the previous public revoke endpoint allowed anyone with a
 217:     plugin UUID to wipe out a plugin. Now sender signs the revoke envelope
 218:     with their Ed25519 private key, and we also verify the row belongs to
 219:     that sender before flipping revoked_at.
 220:     """
 221:     try:
 222:         sender = await get_active_sender(db, payload.sender_id)
 223:     except SenderNotFoundError as exc:
 224:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="sender not found") from exc
 225:     except SenderRevokedError as exc:
 226:         raise HTTPException(status_code=410, detail="sender revoked") from exc
 227: 
 228:     sender_sig = decode_base64(payload.sender_signature, field_name="sender_signature", exact=64)
 229:     if not verify_message_envelope(sender.public_key, _revoke_envelope(payload), sender_sig):
 230:         raise HTTPException(status_code=401, detail="invalid sender signature")
 231: 
 232:     plugin_result = await db.execute(select(Plugin).where(Plugin.id == payload.plugin_row_id))
 233:     plugin = plugin_result.scalar_one_or_none()
 234:     if plugin is None:
 235:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found")
 236:     if plugin.sender_id != payload.sender_id:
 237:         # Don't leak existence of foreign-sender's plugins ג€” 404 not 403.
 238:         raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="plugin not found")
 239:

 355: class PluginLatestResponse(BaseModel):
 356:     plugin_row_id: UUID
 357:     sender_id: UUID
 358:     plugin_identifier: str
 359:     version: str
 360:     signed_bundle_url: str
 361:     manifest_hash: str
 362:     bundle_hash: str
 363:     signature: str
 364:     capabilities: list[str]
 365:     endpoints: list[str]
 366:     created_at: datetime
 367:     # M11.4: when the row is revoked, surface why so devices can render
 368:     # differentiated UX (silent for ``superseded``, security alert for
 369:     # ``compromised``, neutral "unavailable" for ``sender_disabled``).
 370:     # The /latest endpoint filters revoked rows out so these are always
 371:     # null there; the /by-id endpoint (used for historical lookups by
 372:     # plugin_row_id) returns whatever the row's current revoke state is.
 373:     revoked_at: datetime | None = None
 374:     revocation_reason: str | None = None
 375: 
 376: 
 377: # M11.4: classified revocation reasons. Devices use this to decide UX:
 378: # - ``superseded``: silent; show in update prompts.
 379: # - ``compromised``: refuse to execute; show security alert.
 380: # - ``sender_disabled``: stop rendering; show neutral "unavailable".
 381: # - ``unspecified``: legacy revokes (pre-M11.4) where no reason was given;
 382: #   conservative client treats this as ``compromised`` until clarified.
 383: REVOCATION_REASONS = frozenset({"superseded", "compromised", "sender_disabled", "unspecified"})
 384: 
 385: 
 386: class PluginRevokeRequest(BaseModel):
 387:     sender_id: UUID
 388:     plugin_row_id: UUID
 389:     sender_signature: str  # base64 Ed25519 over canonical body
 390:     # Optional in V1 for backwards compatibility with the M8.1 contract;
 391:     # senders SHOULD always supply one. Missing reason ג†’ stored as null;
 392:     # client code interprets null as ``unspecified``.
 393:     reason: str | None = None
 394: 
 395:     @field_validator("sender_signature")
 396:     @classmethod
 397:     def validate_sender_signature(cls, value: str) -> str:
 398:         decode_base64(value, field_name="sender_signature", exact=64)
 399:         return value
 400: 
 401:     @field_validator("reason")
 402:     @classmethod
 403:     def validate_reason(cls, value: str | None) -> str | None:
 404:         if value is None:
 405:             return None
 406:         if value not in REVOCATION_REASONS:
 407:             raise ValueError(
