 250:     suspend fun push(): Result<Unit> = syncMutex.withLock {
 251:         val masterKey = session.sessionState.value.masterKey ?: return@withLock Result.success(Unit)
 252:         // Defensive: a future-schema blob (downloaded by a newer client and
 253:         // somehow persisted on this older one) should NOT be pushed back ג€”
 254:         // we'd write known fields under the future schema_version, losing
 255:         // the V3+ fields the newer client wrote. Refuse-to-push surfaces the
 256:         // version skew as a push failure rather than corrupting state.
 257:         if (_state.value.schemaVersion > EncryptedUserState.SCHEMA_CURRENT) {
 258:             Timber.tag(TAG).w(
 259:                 "refusing to push schema_version %d (client supports %d)",
 260:                 _state.value.schemaVersion, EncryptedUserState.SCHEMA_CURRENT,
 261:             )
 262:             return@withLock Result.failure(IllegalStateException("future schema; refusing to push"))
 263:         }
 264:         runCatching {
 265:             attemptPush(masterKey)
 266:             clearDirty()
 267:         }.onFailure { Timber.tag(TAG).w(it, "push failed (after retry)") }
 268:     }
 269: 
 270:     private suspend fun attemptPush(masterKey: ByteArray) {
 271:         val blob = encodeLocal(_state.value, masterKey)
 272:         val expected = lastKnownRemoteVersion()
 273:         try {
 274:             val response = api.putUserState(
 275:                 StatePutRequestDto(
 276:                     expectedStateVersion = expected,
 277:                     newEncryptedBlob = blob,
 278:                 ),
 279:             )
 280:             if (!response.isSuccessful) {
 281:                 if (response.code() == 409) {
 282:                     handleConflictAndRetry(masterKey)
 283:                 } else {
 284:                     throw HttpException(response)
 285:                 }
 286:             } else {
 287:                 response.body()?.newStateVersion?.let { setLastKnownRemoteVersion(it) }
 288:             }
 289:         } catch (e: HttpException) {
 290:             if (e.code() == 409) handleConflictAndRetry(masterKey) else throw e
 291:         }
 292:     }
 293: 
 294:     private suspend fun handleConflictAndRetry(masterKey: ByteArray) {
 295:         // Server has a newer blob. Pull, merge, re-push exactly once. If the
 296:         // retry also conflicts, give up and rely on the next foreground tick
 297:         // (flushPendingPush will pick it up because the dirty flag is set
 298:         // until push() succeeds).
 299:         val response = api.getUserState()
 300:         val remoteState = decodeRemote(response.encryptedBlob, masterKey)
 301:         val merged = StateMerger.merge(local = _state.value, remote = remoteState)
 302:         _state.value = merged
 303:         persist(merged, remoteVersion = response.stateVersion)
 304: 
 305:         val newBlob = encodeLocal(_state.value, masterKey)
 306:         val retry = api.putUserState(
 307:             StatePutRequestDto(
 308:                 expectedStateVersion = response.stateVersion,
 309:                 newEncryptedBlob = newBlob,
 310:             ),
 311:         )
 312:         if (retry.isSuccessful) {
 313:             retry.body()?.newStateVersion?.let { setLastKnownRemoteVersion(it) }
 314:         } else {
 315:             Timber.tag(TAG).w("CAS retry still conflicted (HTTP %d); will retry later", retry.code())
 316:         }
 317:     }
 318: 
 319:     private fun persist(state: EncryptedUserState, remoteVersion: Int? = null) {
 320:         prefs.edit()
 321:             .putString(KEY_STATE_JSON, state.toJson())
 322:             .apply {
 323:                 if (remoteVersion != null) putInt(KEY_REMOTE_VERSION, remoteVersion)
 324:             }
 325:             .apply()
 326:     }
 327: 
 328:     /**
 329:      * Wipes all persisted state and resets to empty. Invoked automatically
 330:      * on session lock (logout, JWT expiry) ג€” see the init block. Exposed
 331:      * for tests; production code should rely on the session-observer.
 332:      */
 333:     suspend fun clear() = clearInternal()
 334: 
 335:     private suspend fun clearInternal() = syncMutex.withLock {
 336:         _state.value = EncryptedUserState()
 337:         prefs.edit().clear().apply()
 338:     }
 339: 
 340:     private fun loadFromDisk(): EncryptedUserState =
 341:         prefs.getString(KEY_STATE_JSON, null)?.let {
 342:             runCatching { EncryptedUserState.fromJson(it) }.getOrNull()
 343:         } ?: EncryptedUserState()

 345:     private fun lastKnownRemoteVersion(): Int = prefs.getInt(KEY_REMOTE_VERSION, 0)
 346:     private fun setLastKnownRemoteVersion(v: Int) {
 347:         prefs.edit().putInt(KEY_REMOTE_VERSION, v).apply()
 348:     }

 350:     private fun encodeLocal(state: EncryptedUserState, masterKey: ByteArray): String {
 351:         val plaintext = state.toJson().toByteArray(Charsets.UTF_8)
 352:         val wire = Aead.encrypt(masterKey, plaintext)
 353:         return Base64.encodeToString(wire, Base64.NO_WRAP)
 354:     }
 355: 
 356:     private fun decodeRemote(blobB64: String, masterKey: ByteArray): EncryptedUserState {
 357:         if (blobB64.isBlank()) return EncryptedUserState()
 358:         val wire = Base64.decode(blobB64, Base64.NO_WRAP)
 359:         val plaintext = Aead.decrypt(masterKey, wire)
 360:         return EncryptedUserState.fromJson(plaintext.toString(Charsets.UTF_8))
 361:     }

 # Syncler integration guide
 
-You are integrating your app with the Syncler platform. Syncler is a content-blind transport + plugin host: your backend pushes encrypted blobs to a user's phone, and a JavaScript plugin you wrote renders them and handles taps. **Read this end-to-end before writing code; it's ~6 pages.**
+You are integrating your app with the Syncler platform. Syncler is a content-blind transport + plugin host: your backend pushes encrypted blobs to a user's phone, and a JavaScript plugin you wrote renders them and handles taps. **Read this end-to-end before writing code; it's ~7 pages.**
 
 Syncler does not know what your data looks like, what your UI says, or what your buttons do. Your payload, your plugin code, your callback endpoint — Syncler just routes bytes.
 
@@ -11,7 +11,22 @@ Two artifacts:
 1. A **JavaScript plugin** that runs in the Syncler Android app's WebView and renders the **detail view** of a card when the user taps it. The plugin defines buttons that POST back to your backend.
 2. **Backend code** that pushes a card to the user via the Syncler server, and an HTTP endpoint that receives the action callback.
 
-The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, time. The host draws that row from structured metadata you embed in the payload (`hostPreview`, §2). +The Syncler inbox shows a *native* row for every message — sender name, title, subtitle, summary, relative timestamp. The host draws that row from structured metadata you embed in the payload (`hostPreview`, §2). The plugin's `render()` is reserved for the full-screen detail view that appears when the user taps a row.
+
+### What the host does for you
+
+Once a card is in a user's inbox, the host handles all of the following without you doing anything plugin-side:
+
+- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary / timestamp).
+- **Unread indicator** + read sync across the user's devices. A row marks read when the user opens the detail view; the state syncs via an encrypted CAS state blob.
+- **Date buckets** in the chronological view (Today / Yesterday / Earlier).
+- **Group-by-sender** toggle with collapsible sections — the user picks chronological or grouped from the top app bar.
+- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
+- **Archive** + **Delete** + **Multi-select** with bulk Archive / Delete. Archive/delete state is local and synced across devices; deleted messages are hidden from inbox AND archive.
+- **Bottom navigation** (Inbox / Senders / Settings) — the user is always one tap away from your card.
+- **Revocation UX** — if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See §5.5.
+
+You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.

  16: # Semver-lite: MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH[-prerelease]. Reject anything weirder.
  17: # Components capped at 6 digits each so server + client Int parsers agree.
  18: _SEMVER = re.compile(r"^(\d{1,6})\.(\d{1,6})\.(\d{1,6})(?:-[A-Za-z0-9.\-]+)?$")
  19: 
  20: 
  21: class PluginError(Exception):
  22:     """Base."""
  23:

  25: class InvalidVersionError(PluginError):
  26:     """Version string is not valid semver-lite."""
  27: 
  28: 
  29: class VersionRegressionError(PluginError):
  30:     """New version is not strictly greater than the latest published."""
  31: 
  32: 
  33: class DuplicateVersionError(PluginError):
  34:     """(sender_id, plugin_identifier, version) already exists."""

  37: class PluginNotFoundError(PluginError):
  38:     """No plugin with that identifier."""

  41: def _parse_version(version: str) -> tuple[int, int, int, str]:
  42:     match = _SEMVER.match(version)
  43:     if not match:
  44:         raise InvalidVersionError(f"invalid version: {version}")
  45:     major, minor, patch = (int(g) for g in match.groups()[:3])
  46:     pre = match.group(0).partition("-")[2] or "~"  # "~" sorts after any prerelease
  47:     return major, minor, patch, pre
  48:

  51:     db: AsyncSession,
  52:     *,

  54:     plugin_identifier: str,
  55:     version: str,

  57:     bundle_hash: bytes,

  61:     endpoints: list[str],
  62: ) -> Plugin:
  63:     new_key = _parse_version(version)
  64: 
  65:     # Reject if any existing non-revoked version is >= new version.
  66:     existing = await db.execute(
  67:         select(Plugin).where(
  68:             and_(
  69:                 Plugin.sender_id == sender_id,
  70:                 Plugin.plugin_identifier == plugin_identifier,
  71:             ),
  72:         ),
  73:     )
  74:     for row in existing.scalars().all():
  75:         if _parse_version(row.version) >= new_key:
  76:             raise VersionRegressionError(
  77:                 f"new version {version} not greater than existing {row.version}",
  78:             )
  79: 
  80:     plugin = Plugin(
  81:         id=uuid.uuid4(),  # fresh row UUID per published version
  82:         sender_id=sender_id,
  83:         plugin_identifier=plugin_identifier,
  84:         version=version,
  85:         manifest_hash=manifest_hash,

  89:         capabilities=capabilities,
  90:         endpoints=endpoints,
  91:     )
  92:     db.add(plugin)
  93:     try:
  94:         await db.commit()
  95:     except IntegrityError as exc:
  96:         await db.rollback()
  97:         # Narrowed: only re-classify the UNIQUE-specific case as a 409
  98:         # duplicate. Other IntegrityErrors (FK violations etc) escape
  99:         # to the route handler as 500s so we see actual schema bugs.
 100:         msg = str(exc.orig) if exc.orig else str(exc)
 101:         if "uq_plugins_sender_identifier_version" in msg:
 102:             raise DuplicateVersionError(
 103:                 f"plugin {plugin_identifier} version {version} already exists",
 104:             ) from exc
 105:         raise
 106:     await db.refresh(plugin)
 107:     return plugin

 118:                 Plugin.revoked_at.is_(None),

 121:     )

 123:     if not rows:

 129: async def get_plugin_by_id(
 130:     db: AsyncSession, *, plugin_row_id: uuid.UUID
 131: ) -> Plugin:
 132:     """Returns the plugin row whether or not it's revoked. Used by the
 133:     device's historical lookup path so an old message can re-resolve the
 134:     exact bundle it was originally validated against, even after the
 135:     sender published a newer (or a revoked) version under the same
 136:     plugin_identifier.
 137: 
 138:     Raises PluginNotFoundError if the row doesn't exist at all.
 139:     """
 140:     result = await db.execute(select(Plugin).where(Plugin.id == plugin_row_id))
 141:     plugin = result.scalar_one_or_none()
 142:     if plugin is None:
 143:         raise PluginNotFoundError(f"no plugin row {plugin_row_id}")
 144:     return plugin

 146: 
 147: # M11.4: severity ordering for monotonic revocation-reason updates. Only an
 148: # UP-traversal of this list is allowed once a row is revoked, so a sender
 149: # (or a compromised sender's key) cannot later silently downgrade a
 150: # `compromised` revoke to `superseded` and trick devices into running
 151: # untrusted code.
 152: _REASON_SEVERITY = {
 153:     None: 0,
 154:     "superseded": 1,
 155:     "sender_disabled": 2,
 156:     "unspecified": 2,
 157:     "compromised": 3,
 158: }
 159: 
 160: 
 161: async def revoke_plugin_row(
 162:     db: AsyncSession,
 163:     plugin_row_id: uuid.UUID,
 164:     reason: str | None = None,
 165: ) -> Plugin:
 166:     """Mark a plugin row revoked, optionally with a classification reason.
 167: 
 168:     Idempotent on `revoked_at` ג€” re-revoking does NOT push the timestamp
 169:     forward. The reason field is monotonic: a higher-severity reason can
 170:     overwrite a lower one (so `superseded` ג†’ `compromised` works when a
 171:     vuln surfaces in an already-superseded version), but the reverse
 172:     silently no-ops so a leaked sender key can't downgrade a security
 173:     revoke into a harmless one.
 174:     """
 175:     result = await db.execute(select(Plugin).where(Plugin.id == plugin_row_id))
 176:     plugin = result.scalar_one_or_none()
 177:     if plugin is None:
 178:         raise PluginNotFoundError(f"no plugin row {plugin_row_id}")
 179:     changed = False
 180:     if plugin.revoked_at is None:
 181:         plugin.revoked_at = datetime.now(UTC)
 182:         changed = True
 183:     if reason is not None:
 184:         current_sev = _REASON_SEVERITY.get(plugin.revocation_reason, 0)
 185:         new_sev = _REASON_SEVERITY.get(reason, 0)
 186:         if new_sev > current_sev:
 187:             plugin.revocation_reason = reason
 188:             changed = True
 189:     if changed:
 190:         await db.commit()
 191:         await db.refresh(plugin)
 192:     return plugin
 193: 
 194: 
 195: def _to_uuid(value: Any) -> uuid.UUID:
 196:     if isinstance(value, uuid.UUID):
 197:         return value
 198:     return uuid.UUID(str(value))

.\docs\integration-guide.md:297:- **`401 invalid envelope signature`** — your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:298:- **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** — `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see §5 vs §6).
.\docs\integration-guide.md:299:- **`410 recipient has no active devices`** — the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:300:- **`409 nonce already used`** — your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:301:- **`429 rate limited`** — back off + retry per `Retry-After` header.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:302:- **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch — missing registerPlugin() call?"** — your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See §3.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:303:- **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** — your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.
.\docs\integration-guide.md:304:- **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** — caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see §2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters — emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.

   3: import org.json.JSONObject

   5: /**
   6:  * Builds the per-card WebView HTML shell.
   7:  *
   8:  * The shell:
   9:  *  1. Installs a `window.platform` proxy that round-trips through the native
  10:  *     `__syncler_native__` JavascriptInterface (see [CardBridge]). For V1
  11:  *     inbox mode only `platform.network.fetch` is wired native-side; other
  12:  *     methods reject with a clear error so plugins fail visibly rather than
  13:  *     silently no-op'ing.
  14:  *  2. Runs the plugin bundle (IIFE; self-registers via `registerPlugin(...)`).
  15:  *  3. Dispatches the `render` hook with the message payload, injects the
  16:  *     returned HTML into the body, and re-creates any inline `<script>` tags
  17:  *     so click handlers (e.g. lottery's "Played" button) wire up.
  18:  */
  19: internal object RenderShell {
  20:     fun build(bundleJs: String, payloadJson: String): String {
  21:         // Defensive: the bundle's source may contain literal `</script>` (e.g.
  22:         // in a quoted string). Break the sequence so the host's `<script>`
  23:         // closer doesn't get prematurely matched by the HTML parser.
  24:         val safeBundle = bundleJs.replace("</script", "<\\/script", ignoreCase = true)
  25:         val safePayloadWrap = JSONObject().put("p", payloadJson).toString()
  26:             .replace("</script", "<\\/script", ignoreCase = true)
  27:         return """
  28:             <!doctype html>
  29:             <html>
  30:             <head>
  31:               <meta charset="utf-8">
  32:               <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width,initial-scale=1">
  33:               <style>
  34:                 html, body { margin: 0; padding: 0; }
  35:                 body { font-family: -apple-system, Roboto, sans-serif; color: #1c1b1f; background: transparent; }
  36:                 #syncler-render-error { color: #b3261e; padding: 12px; font-size: 13px; }
  37:               </style>
  38:             </head>
  39:             <body>
  40:               <script>
  41:               // Capture uncaught errors that fire during bundle execution.
  42:               // WebView <script> tags swallow throws and move on to the next
  43:               // block, so without this hook a manifest-validation failure (or
  44:               // any other top-level throw) is invisible ג€” the symptom you'd
  45:               // see is the *next* error ("No Syncler plugin has been
  46:               // registered") instead of the real root cause.
  47:               window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors = [];
  48:               window.addEventListener('error', (ev) => {
  49:                 window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors.push(
  50:                   (ev.error && ev.error.message) || ev.message || 'unknown error'
  51:                 );
  52:               });
  53:               window.addEventListener('unhandledrejection', (ev) => {
  54:                 const reason = ev.reason;
  55:                 window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors.push(
  56:                   (reason && reason.message) || String(reason)
  57:                 );
  58:               });
  59:               </script>
  60:               <script>
  61:               (() => {
  62:                 const callbacks = new Map();
  63:                 let nextCallbackId = 1;
  64:                 window.__syncler_internal_callback = (callbackId, result) => {
  65:                   const callback = callbacks.get(callbackId);
  66:                   if (!callback) return;
  67:                   callbacks.delete(callbackId);
  68:                   if (result && result.success) callback.resolve(result.value);
  69:                   else callback.reject(new Error((result && (result.message || result.error)) || 'unknown_error'));
  70:                 };
  71:                 const nativeCall = (method, args) => new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
  72:                   const callbackId = String(nextCallbackId++);
  73:                   callbacks.set(callbackId, { resolve, reject });
  74:                   window.__syncler_native__.call(method, JSON.stringify(args || {}), callbackId);
  75:                 });
  76:                 const asResponse = async (payload) => new Response(payload.body || '', {
  77:                   status: payload.status || 200,
  78:                   headers: payload.headers || {}
  79:                 });
  80:                 const reject = (name) => () => Promise.reject(new Error(
  81:                   'platform.' + name + ' is not wired in V1 inbox mode'));
  82:                 window.platform = {
  83:                   __version__: '1.0.0',
  84:                   showNotification: reject('showNotification'),
  85:                   storage: { get: reject('storage.get'), set: reject('storage.set'), delete: reject('storage.delete') },
  86:                   network: {
  87:                     fetch: (url, init) => nativeCall('platform.network.fetch', { url, init }).then(asResponse)
  88:                   },
  89:                   camera: { capture: reject('camera.capture') },
  90:                   gallery: { pick: reject('gallery.pick') },
  91:                   file: { pick: reject('file.pick') },
  92:                   location: { current: reject('location.current') },
  93:                   message: {
  94:                     respond: reject('message.respond'),
  95:                     dismissBehavior: () => undefined
  96:                   }
  97:                 };
  98:               })();
  99:               </script>
 100:               <script>$safeBundle</script>
 101:               <script>
 102:               (async () => {
 103:                 try {
 104:                   // If the bundle threw at load time, surface that ג€” its real
 105:                   // message is far more useful than the generic
 106:                   // "plugin not registered" we'd otherwise see.
 107:                   const loadErrors = window.__syncler_bundleLoadErrors || [];
 108:                   if (loadErrors.length > 0) {
 109:                     throw new Error('plugin bundle threw at load: ' + loadErrors.join(' | '));
 110:                   }
 111:                   const payloadWrap = $safePayloadWrap;
 112:                   const payload = JSON.parse(payloadWrap.p);
 113:                   const dispatcher = window.__syncler_internal_dispatch;
 114:                   if (typeof dispatcher !== 'function') {
 115:                     throw new Error('plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch ג€” missing registerPlugin() call?');
 116:                   }
 117:                   const html = await dispatcher('render', [payload]);
 118:                   if (typeof html !== 'string') {
 119:                     throw new Error('plugin render() did not return a string');
 120:                   }
 121:                   document.body.innerHTML = html;
 122:                   document.body.querySelectorAll('script').forEach((oldScript) => {
 123:                     const newScript = document.createElement('script');
 124:                     for (const attr of oldScript.attributes) newScript.setAttribute(attr.name, attr.value);
 125:                     newScript.textContent = oldScript.textContent;
 126:                     oldScript.parentNode.replaceChild(newScript, oldScript);
 127:                   });
 128:                 } catch (e) {
 129:                   document.body.innerHTML =
 130:                     '<div id="syncler-render-error">render failed: ' +
 131:                     (e && e.message ? e.message : String(e)) + '</div>';
 132:                 }
 133:               })();
 134:               </script>
 135:             </body>
 136:             </html>
 137:         """.trimIndent()
 138:     }

   1: package app.syncler.feature.inbox
   2: 
   3: import android.webkit.JavascriptInterface
   4: import android.webkit.WebView
   5: import app.syncler.feature.inbox.BuildConfig
   6: import kotlinx.coroutines.CoroutineScope
   7: import kotlinx.coroutines.Dispatchers
   8: import kotlinx.coroutines.SupervisorJob
   9: import kotlinx.coroutines.cancel
  10: import kotlinx.coroutines.launch
  11: import kotlinx.coroutines.withContext
  12: import okhttp3.ConnectionSpec
  13: import okhttp3.CookieJar
  14: import okhttp3.MediaType.Companion.toMediaTypeOrNull
  15: import okhttp3.OkHttpClient
  16: import okhttp3.Request
  17: import okhttp3.RequestBody.Companion.toRequestBody
  18: import org.json.JSONObject
  19: 
  20: /**
  21:  * Minimal native bridge for inbox-rendered cards. Exposed to the WebView as
  22:  * `window.__syncler_native__`; the shell HTML wraps it in a `window.platform`
  23:  * proxy that mirrors the SDK contract.
  24:  *
  25:  * Only `platform.network.fetch` is wired ג€” the lottery dogfood's "Played"
  26:  * button needs it, and that's the only capability V1 senders rely on. Other
  27:  * methods (storage, camera, notifications, ג€¦) explicitly reject so plugins
  28:  * fail loudly instead of silently no-op'ing. Wiring the full bridge is the
  29:  * next chunk, and it should reuse `:feature:plugin-host`'s bridges rather
  30:  * than re-implement them here.
  31:  */
  32: class CardBridge(
  33:     private val webView: WebView,
  34:     private val declaredEndpoints: List<String>,
  35: ) {
  36:     private val scope = CoroutineScope(SupervisorJob() + Dispatchers.IO)
  37:     private val httpClient = OkHttpClient.Builder()
  38:         .cookieJar(CookieJar.NO_COOKIES)
  39:         .connectionSpecs(
  40:             if (BuildConfig.DEBUG) {
  41:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS, ConnectionSpec.CLEARTEXT)
  42:             } else {
  43:                 listOf(ConnectionSpec.MODERN_TLS)
  44:             },
  45:         )
  46:         .build()
  47: 
  48:     @JavascriptInterface
  49:     fun call(method: String, argsJson: String, callbackId: String) {
  50:         scope.launch {
  51:             val result = runCatching { dispatch(method, argsJson) }
  52:             val payload = if (result.isSuccess) {
  53:                 """{"success":true,"value":${result.getOrThrow()}}"""
  54:             } else {
  55:                 val message = result.exceptionOrNull()?.message ?: "card bridge error"
  56:                 """{"success":false,"error":"call_failed","message":${JSONObject.quote(message)}}"""
  57:             }
  58:             webView.post {
  59:                 webView.evaluateJavascript(
  60:                     "window.__syncler_internal_callback(${JSONObject.quote(callbackId)}, $payload)",
  61:                     null,
  62:                 )
  63:             }
  64:         }
  65:     }
  66: 
  67:     fun destroy() {
  68:         scope.cancel()
  69:     }
  70: 
  71:     private suspend fun dispatch(method: String, argsJson: String): String = when (method) {
  72:         "platform.network.fetch" -> doFetch(argsJson)
  73:         else -> throw UnsupportedOperationException("$method is not wired in inbox mode")
  74:     }
  75: 
  76:     private suspend fun doFetch(argsJson: String): String = withContext(Dispatchers.IO) {
  77:         val args = JSONObject(argsJson)
  78:         val url = args.optString("url").ifBlank { throw IllegalArgumentException("missing url") }
  79:         // Scheme check (defense in depth ג€” the OkHttp client already refuses
  80:         // cleartext in release via its connectionSpecs, but failing explicitly
  81:         // here gives a clearer error and survives future client wiring drift).
  82:         val schemeOk = url.startsWith("https://") || (BuildConfig.DEBUG && url.startsWith("http://"))
  83:         if (!schemeOk) throw SecurityException("fetch URL must be HTTPS: $url")
  84:         if (!matchesAny(url, declaredEndpoints)) {
  85:             throw SecurityException("endpoint not declared: $url")
  86:         }
  87:         val init = args.optJSONObject("init")
  88:         val method = init?.optString("method")?.uppercase()?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() } ?: "GET"
  89:         val bodyText = init?.optString("body")?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() && method !in setOf("GET", "HEAD") }
  90:         val mediaType = init?.optString("contentType")?.takeIf { it.isNotBlank() }?.toMediaTypeOrNull()
  91:         val request = Request.Builder().url(url).method(method, bodyText?.toRequestBody(mediaType)).apply {
  92:             init?.optJSONObject("headers")?.let { headers ->
  93:                 headers.keys().forEach { key -> header(key, headers.optString(key)) }
  94:             }
  95:         }.build()
  96: 
  97:         httpClient.newCall(request).execute().use { response ->
  98:             val responseBody = response.body?.string().orEmpty()
  99:             val headersJson = JSONObject().also { h ->
 100:                 response.headers.names().forEach { name ->
 101:                     h.put(name, response.headers(name).joinToString(","))
 102:                 }
 103:             }
 104:             JSONObject()
 105:                 .put("status", response.code)
 106:                 .put("headers", headersJson)
 107:                 .put("body", responseBody)
 108:                 .toString()
 109:         }
 110:     }
 111: 
 112:     private fun matchesAny(url: String, patterns: List<String>): Boolean =
 113:         patterns.any { pattern -> endpointPatternToRegex(pattern).matches(url) }
 114: 
 115:     // Same logic as :feature:plugin-host's EndpointMatcher; inlined here so
 116:     // :feature:inbox doesn't need to depend on the whole plugin-host module
 117:     // graph just for this glob match.
 118:     private fun endpointPatternToRegex(pattern: String): Regex {
 119:         val pathStart = findPathStart(pattern)
 120:         val source = buildString {
 121:             pattern.forEachIndexed { index, character ->
 122:                 if (character == '*') {
 123:                     append(if (index < pathStart) "[^./]*" else "[^/]*")
 124:                 } else {
 125:                     append(Regex.escape(character.toString()))
 126:                 }
 127:             }
 128:         }
 129:         return Regex("^$source$")
 130:     }
 131: 
 132:     private fun findPathStart(pattern: String): Int {
 133:         val schemeEnd = pattern.indexOf("://")
 134:         val searchFrom = if (schemeEnd == -1) 0 else schemeEnd + 3
 135:         val slash = pattern.indexOf('/', searchFrom)
 136:         return if (slash == -1) pattern.length else slash
 137:     }
 138: 
 139:     companion object {
 140:         const val NATIVE_BRIDGE_NAME = "__syncler_native__"
 141:     }
 142: }

The current implementation confirms the key mechanics: read marks only in `open()`, bundle lookup uses `/v1/plugins/by-id/{plugin_row_id}`, archive/delete are CAS-backed filters, and dismiss exists only as a server/API path. I’m now reading the original consultation summaries to classify intentional exceptions versus drift.

**Core Stance**

The inbox should stop treating each message as ג€a little app embedded in a scrolling list.ג€ That is the wrong primitive. The actual product primitive is:

**host-owned inbox item, plugin-owned detail surface.**

The host should own the list, unread state, grouping, archive, expiration, selection, empty/error states, and app chrome. Plugins should own the rich rendering and domain-specific interaction once the user opens a message or enters a plugin-owned surface. That gives you a usable inbox without letting arbitrary plugins fragment the core app into multiple competing UX systems.

The current fixed `280 dp` WebView is not merely the wrong height. It is the wrong contract. A rich card with twenty lines of detail, summary, and buttons does not belong inline in a feed. Auto-growing it would make the feed unusable. Nested scroll would make gesture behavior poor. Letting the plugin dynamically claim height would turn the host list into a layout negotiation protocol with untrusted, asynchronous documents. That path gets fragile quickly.

The next UX should have two levels:

1. **Inbox preview row/card**, owned by the host.
2. **Message detail view**, rendered by the plugin in a WebView.

The preview should be compact, predictable, and scannable: sender/plugin identity, time, title, short summary, unread marker, status/error affordance, maybe one primary action if the plugin declares it safe. The detail view is where the current plugin HTML belongs.

If you ship only one change next, ship this: **tap a message to open a full-height detail view, and make the inbox list a compact host-owned preview list.** Everything else improves once that is true.

**Card Presentation**

Fixed-height inline WebViews are useful for proving the bridge. They are not a product UX. The host should own inbox height. In the list, each item should have stable dimensions. I would allow two preview density classes, not arbitrary height:

- `compact`: about one to three lines of content plus metadata.
- `expandedPreview`: maybe up to six lines for genuinely useful summaries.

The plugin should not be able to say ג€I am 842 px tall, resize me.ג€ That is fine in a detail surface, not in the inbox. Measurement-on-render and ג€done renderingג€ callbacks are especially dangerous because they couple list virtualization, WebView lifecycle, and untrusted content timing. The UX will jitter, scroll positions will jump, and failures become layout bugs.

The plugin contract should instead separate **preview model** from **detail renderer**.

A message should carry encrypted, client-visible host metadata, produced by the sender/plugin SDK:

```json
{
  "title": "Draw results ready",
  "subtitle": "Powerball May 21",
  "summary": "3 matched lines, best prize $50",
  "priority": "normal",
  "category": "results",
  "previewStyle": "compact",
  "searchText": ["powerball", "draw", "may 21", "ticket 1842"]
}
```

The host renders that natively. Then the detail WebView gets the full payload and plugin bundle. This is the clean boundary: the server remains content-blind, but the client can use decrypted metadata.

I would still allow optional plugin-rendered preview later, but not as the default. If you allow it, constrain it brutally: fixed host-provided viewport, no dynamic height, no network during preview render unless explicitly allowed, no arbitrary chrome, no assumption that it appears for every row. The first usable version should not depend on WebView-per-row at all.

**Read / Unread**

Read state is UX state, not delivery state. Do not put it in server `delivery_status` except perhaps as a coarse transport/debug signal. ג€Delivered,ג€ ג€fetched,ג€ ג€decrypted,ג€ ג€rendered,ג€ and ג€readג€ are different events.

Read/unread should live in the encrypted multi-device user-state blob from M7. That gives you cross-device sync without making the server content-aware. The record can be keyed by message id:

```json
{
  "messages": {
    "<message_id>": {
      "readAt": "...",
      "archivedAt": "...",
      "starred": false,
      "dismissedAt": null
    }
  }
}
```

Marking something read should be conservative. Do not mark read just because it appeared in the list. That punishes scanning. I would mark read when:

- the user opens the detail view,
- the user invokes a meaningful action from the preview,
- the user explicitly marks as read,
- or the plugin requests `markRead()` during detail view after a host-approved event.

That last one matters for chat-style or ticket-style plugins, where the detail view may have its own ג€seenג€ semantics. But the host should still mediate it.

Visual treatment should be boring and strong: unread dot, heavier title, maybe a small unread count in date/plugin filters. Avoid giant blue backgrounds or card chrome that makes the whole inbox noisy. ג€Unreadג€ is a state, not the main content.

Sync should happen across devices. If I open a lottery result on the phone, the tablet should not keep shouting that it is new. CAS conflicts are acceptable if the state model is mergeable. For message UI state, use per-message timestamps and tombstones so merges are deterministic.

**Organization**

The default should be a chronological inbox with date buckets:

- Today
- Yesterday
- Earlier
- Expiring soon, if retention makes that important

Then add lightweight host filters: all, unread, starred/pinned, archived, maybe plugin/sender chips. I would not start with bottom-nav tabs per plugin. That makes the app feel like a plugin launcher instead of an inbox, and it breaks down when one plugin is chat-like, another is alert-like, and another is a dashboard.

Grouped-by-plugin collapsible sections sound appealing for lottery because the domain is discrete. They are worse for notification streams, trading bots, and chat-like senders where recency matters more than plugin identity. Use plugin grouping as a filter or secondary view, not the primary hierarchy.

Pinned/starred is worth having, but not before archive/read/detail. Date buckets are cheap and broadly useful. Plugin-owned mini-tabs inside detail are acceptable because once the user is inside a message/plugin surface, domain organization is the pluginג€™s job.

My preferred navigation:

- **Inbox**: active messages, chronological, host-owned.
- **Archive**: retained local history, host-owned.
- **Devices/Settings**: pairing, senders, plugin permissions, account/session.

Do not add a plugin tab bar yet. If plugins later register durable sections, they can appear behind a ג€Pluginsג€ or ג€Sourcesג€ area, not as peers to Inbox on day one.

**Search**

The userג€™s instinct that ג€search may be implemented by the pluginג€ is half right, but dangerous as the only model.

There are three searches:

1. **Host metadata search**: sender, plugin id/name, title, subtitle, summary, sent-at, unread/archive/starred.
2. **Local decrypted message search**: host-indexed `searchText` supplied by the plugin/sender.
3. **Plugin remote search**: plugin queries its backend and renders results.

The right V1 boundary is hybrid, with host search first.

The host should provide a global search box that always works over local metadata. Because the server is content-blind, the index is local and built after decrypt. The plugin should be able to supply search tokens or a plain text search blob in the encrypted payload. That gives users a reliable search for ג€Powerball,ג€ ג€ticket,ג€ ג€AAPL,ג€ ג€withdrawal,ג€ or ג€Aliceג€ without waking every plugin.

Plugin-side remote search should be an optional extension, not the core inbox search. It is useful for domains where the inbox is only a notification layer over a larger backend: trading history, old chat messages, ticket databases, dashboards. But if search only works when the plugin opts in and its backend is available, the host inbox feels broken. Also, plugin-rendered search results raise navigation questions: are they inbox messages, remote entities, or plugin pages?

I would define:

- Host search returns local messages.
- Plugins may register a `searchProvider`.
- Results are visually separated as ג€From this deviceג€ and ג€From plugin/service.ג€
- Remote plugin results open plugin-owned detail/history surfaces, not fake inbox messages unless the sender actually emitted a message.

That preserves the inbox as a reliable local object while letting richer plugins grow.

**Plugin Role Expansion**

The smallest expansion that makes rich plugins usable is not ג€plugins own tabs.ג€ It is:

1. Plugins provide structured preview metadata.
2. Plugins own message detail rendering.
3. Plugins can request host-mediated actions and state changes from detail.

That is enough for lottery, trading alerts, notification cards, and many workflow senders.

Next, I would allow a plugin-owned **history/detail section** only after the host has stable Inbox and Archive concepts. A plugin could register:

- `messageDetail`
- `settings`
- `history`
- `compose` or `newRequest`
- maybe `dashboard`

But the host must keep the app chrome. Plugins can own content panes, not global navigation rules. They should not be able to replace the top app bar, hide archive/read controls, spoof pairing UI, or create their own permission prompts. The plugin can ask the host to show chrome actions: `markUnread`, `archive`, `openSettings`, `compose`, `refresh`, but the host renders them.

The line I would draw: plugins can own surfaces; the host owns containment, navigation, identity, and trust signals.

**Lifecycle**

Retention changes the UX. A 30-day server cap means the app needs an explicit distinction between server-backed inbox and local history.

I would use:

- **Inbox**: active, unarchived messages not expired locally.
- **Archive**: user-kept local messages.
- **Delete**: remove local copy and dismiss from server if still present.
- **Auto-expire**: server removes after cap; client may keep archived/read copies according to local policy.

Dismissal should map to server cleanup, not necessarily user deletion. If the user archives a message, I would dismiss it from server once safely stored locally, because the server is just delivery/retention. If the user deletes it, remove local state and call dismiss. If the user marks read, do not dismiss automatically unless the product explicitly defines inbox as ephemeral.

For `DISMISS_ALL`, be careful. It is useful for ג€clear all delivered transport items,ג€ but a visible UI action named ג€Delete allג€ or ג€Clear inboxג€ must communicate local consequences. I would start with per-message archive/delete and batch archive, not expose broad dismissal protocol language.

Client persistence longer than 30 days is valuable, especially for lottery and trading. But the plugin bundle question matters: if rendering old messages depends on a bundle that was revoked or unavailable, history breaks. Store the verified bundle version used for the message, or store a stable render artifact/manifest reference. At minimum, cache bundles by hash, not just plugin latest.

**App Chrome**

Use conventional app chrome:

- Top app bar: title/search, account/sync status, overflow.
- Bottom nav: Inbox, Archive, Devices or Settings.
- Optional FAB only if there is at least one installed/paired plugin with a host-declared compose capability.

The chrome can be plugin-aware, but only through host-declared capabilities. For example, a trading bot might expose ג€New alert,ג€ a chat plugin might expose ג€New message,ג€ lottery might expose nothing. If multiple plugins expose compose, the FAB opens a chooser. If none do, no FAB.

Do not put Pair sender / Devices / Refresh / Log out as top-row buttons in the main steady-state UI. Pairing is an onboarding/settings action. Refresh can be pull-to-refresh or overflow. Log out belongs in account/settings. Devices belongs in bottom nav or settings.

**Edge Cases**

These need first-class screens/states, not logs.

Empty inbox after fresh install should say, in product terms, that there are no messages yet and offer Pair sender. After pairing, the empty state should change: ג€Waiting for messages from Xג€ with last poll/sync status available somewhere quiet.

Plugin fetch failed should still show a host preview if metadata decrypted. The row opens an error detail with retry, plugin id/version/hash, and safe diagnostic text. The user should be able to archive/delete without the plugin rendering.

Plugin render threw should not destroy the message. Show host metadata plus ג€Plugin failed to render this message,ג€ with retry and report/copy diagnostics if you have that flow.

Bundle revoked since storage is tricky. Revocation should prevent fetching/executing newly untrusted bundles. It should not automatically make old local history unreadable unless the revocation reason is severe. You need revocation classes: superseded, compromised, sender-disabled. Compromised may require blocking execution and showing a security state.

Payload does not validate against current plugin version: do not use current plugin version. Use the messageג€™s declared plugin id, version/range, bundle hash, and schema. If the exact compatible bundle is unavailable, show a compatibility error and preserve the message.

**Lottery Versus Other Senders**

Lottery wants rich, inspectable result details. It benefits from archive, date buckets, search by draw/ticket, and full detail views. It probably does not need compose, chat, or high-frequency unread behavior.

A trading bot is more time-sensitive and risk-sensitive. It needs priority, freshness, maybe pinned alerts, quick actions, audit history, and stronger stale-state warnings. A trading alert from 27 minutes ago may be materially different from a lottery result from yesterday. It may also need plugin remote search/history because the backend has orders, fills, and account state beyond messages.

A notification sender wants glanceability and bulk management. It may never need heavy detail. For it, host-native previews, archive, unread, and filters matter most.

A chat-style sender breaks the ג€cardג€ metaphor. It wants conversation grouping, sender identity, read receipts, compose, and thread-level navigation. That is exactly why the host should not hard-code plugin grouping as the main inbox model. The host can support a message detail or plugin section that becomes a conversation view, but the global inbox should remain a sane notification surface.

**SDK / Contract Changes**

I would add these plugin/message contract pieces:

- `hostPreview` in encrypted message payload: title, subtitle, summary, optional image/icon token, category, priority, search text, preview density.
- `messageSchemaVersion` and `minPluginVersion`/`maxPluginVersion` or exact compatible bundle hash.
- `surfaces` in plugin manifest: `messageDetail`, optional `previewRenderer`, optional `settings`, optional `history`, optional `compose`, optional `searchProvider`.
- `capabilities` in manifest: network in detail, network in preview, storage, compose, remoteSearch, suggested chrome actions.
- `lifecycle` hooks: `onMessageDetailMount`, `onMessageDetailUnmount`, `onActionResult`, maybe `onHostStateChanged`.
- Host APIs: `platform.message.markRead`, `markUnread`, `archive`, `delete`, `dismissRemote`, `setTitle` only within detail if allowed, `openExternal` with host confirmation, `requestRefresh`.
- Search API: `plugin.search(query, cursor)` returning typed results, with host-rendered result shells and plugin-owned result detail.
- Error contract: plugin can emit validation failure with user-safe message and diagnostic code.

**Architecture Blockers**

The current WebView-per-card model quietly precludes the direction if it remains the only renderer. The list needs to be host-native first, with WebView moved primarily to detail. You can keep WebView-per-preview as an optional constrained path later, but not as the foundation.

The ג€latest bundleג€ fetch model also conflicts with durable history. Old messages must render against the bundle/version/hash they were validated for, or fail gracefully. Cache by SHA-256 and retain manifest metadata per message.

The native bridge currently only has `platform.network.fetch` in inbox mode. Detail surfaces need lifecycle and host state APIs, but those APIs must be narrow and auditable. Do not expand by handing plugins general navigation control.

Finally, the M7 state merger needs to be good enough for message UI state. Read/archive/star/delete are not cache fluff. They need timestamped, mergeable records with tombstones, or multi-device UX will feel random.

The product should become an inbox first and a plugin host second. That does not make plugins weak. It gives them the right place to be powerful: inside detail, history, compose, and dashboard surfaces, contained by host chrome that users can trust.

 succeeded in 286ms:
Here is an independent, opinionated UX direction for Syncler's next iteration.

# The Vision: Syncler as a Managed Micro-App Host

The current UX is a feed of raw E2EE messages. The next iteration must shift from "a secure inbox of dynamic cards" to a **managed host of micro-apps**. We are not building an email client; we are building a zero-trust, multi-device dashboard where senders can push actionable UI to the user's pocket. 

To achieve this, we have to establish a hard boundary between **what the host owns** (hierarchy, navigation, metadata search, global state sync) and **what the plugin owns** (content rendering, detailed interaction, and local storage state). The host must not try to parse content, and the plugin must not be allowed to escape its sandbox to dominate the user's screen space.

### 1. Card Presentation: The Preview-Detail Split
**Stance: Max-height limit with a strictly enforced Host-controlled Detail View.**

Plugins should not own their height unconditionally. Unbounded auto-grow destroys scroll performance and allows malicious/buggy plugins to hijack the screen. Conversely, a fixed 280dp height makes rich plugins unusable.

The solution is a **two-tier rendering model**:
1. **Preview Mode (Inline Card):** The plugin renders in a constrained context. The host enforces a max-height (e.g., `320dp`). If the plugin's content overflows, it clips, but the host overlays a standard "Tap to Expand" affordance over the bottom edge.
2. **Detail Mode (Full Screen/Modal):** When the user taps the card, the host launches a new full-screen `AndroidView(WebView)` for that specific card. The plugin is passed a runtime flag indicating it is now in `detail` mode and has the entire vertical viewport.

This gives plugins the space they need for rich interactions (e.g., charting for a trading bot) while keeping the primary feed scannable. 

### 2. Read/Unread State: The Silent Signal
**Stance: Client-local authority, synced via the M7 encrypted CAS blob.**

Because the server is E2EE content-blind, it cannot reliably infer "read" state based on content semantics. A card transitions to "read" when:
- It is explicitly interacted with (an action button is pressed).
- It is opened in the Detail View.
- It dwells fully visible in the viewport for $> 3$ seconds.

This state is stored locally in SQLite and patched into the M7 encrypted user-state blob. When the user opens their tablet, it pulls the CAS blob, decrypts it, and marks the corresponding `message_id`s as read locally. Visually, unread cards have a subtle host-rendered accent (e.g., a left-border color bar). Plugins are *unaware* of their read state; this is strictly host chrome.

### 3. Organization: The Grouped Inbox
**Stance: Flat list by date for the Inbox, with a dedicated Plugin Dashboard for structured access.**

A pure folder-by-sender approach hides time-sensitive alerts, but a flat list becomes a chaotic feed. We need both:
- **The Inbox (Timeline):** Cards are ordered by `sentAt`. However, consecutive cards from the *same plugin* within a short time window (e.g., 2 hours) are visually collapsed into a "stack" by the host. Only the latest card is fully rendered in Preview Mode; the rest are represented by a host UI footer: "3 more from [Sender]".
- **The Dashboard (Per-Plugin View):** The app structure needs a Bottom Nav. The second tab is "Plugins". This shows a directory of paired plugins. Tapping a plugin opens a host-managed screen showing *only* cards for that plugin, bypassing the Inbox noise.

### 4. Search: The Federated Model
**Stance: Host does metadata search; Plugin does content search (Opt-in).**

The host cannot do full-text search because the payloads are E2EE and only decrypted just-in-time. Relying entirely on a plugin-implemented global search is too complex for UI handoffs. 
- **Global Search:** The host provides a search bar at the top of the Inbox. This searches *only* host metadata: Sender Name, Plugin Name, and Date.
- **Plugin-Level Search:** If the user navigates to a specific plugin's Dashboard, and the plugin manifest declares `Capability.SEARCH`, the host provides a search bar and forwards the query to the plugin via a new bridge hook `__syncler_internal_dispatch('onSearch', query)`. The plugin then renders its own results using its local `platform.storage`.

### 5. Plugin Role Expansion: The Dedicated Surface
**Stance: Plugins get one extra surfaceג€”the "App View"ג€”but no chrome control.**

V1 plugins own the card render. The next logical expansion is allowing a plugin to own a full-screen view independent of a specific message payload. If a plugin declares `Capability.APP_VIEW`, the host adds a persistent entry for it in the "Plugins" tab. When tapped, the host loads the plugin's JS bundle with a `null` payload. The plugin uses this space to render settings, global stats, or history, pulling data from its `platform.storage`. We draw a hard line: plugins do *not* get to manipulate host chrome (no changing the TopAppBar, no adding custom FABs).

### 6. Lifecycle: Local Expiry & Archive
**Stance: Auto-expire by default, explicit Archive for permanence.**

The server caps retention at 30 days. The client should mirror this to prevent unbounded SQLite bloat. 
- **Dismiss vs Archive:** Swiping a card in the Inbox "Dismisses" it (moves it out of the view, marks it read, keeps it in DB until 30 days, sends `DISMISS` back to sender). If the user wants to keep a receipt forever, the host provides an "Archive" host-action. Archived cards bypass the 30-day GC.
- **Plugin-Driven Expiry:** A plugin can use `platform.message.dismissBehavior` to explicitly retract a message earlier based on user interaction.

### 7. App Chrome: Standardizing the Navigation
**Stance: Standard Material 3 Bottom Nav.**
- **Inbox:** The timeline feed (with unread badges).
- **Plugins:** The directory of paired senders and their dedicated full-screen views.
- **Settings:** Device management, pair new sender, log out.
No FAB. A "Compose" affordance doesn't make sense globally because the user doesn't initiate messages to arbitrary plugins; they *respond* to E2EE pushes.

### 8. Edge Cases
- **Fresh-pair "What do I do now":** Upon pairing a new sender, the host injects a synthetic, host-generated card: "Paired with [Sender]. Waiting for their first push..." This prevents empty-state confusion.
- **Plugin fetch failed / render threw:** The current `PayloadFallbackView` is good, but it should be framed as a graceful error state on the card: "Plugin failed to load. [View Raw Data] [Retry]".
- **Revoked bundles / Invalid signatures:** If a bundle hash changes maliciously, the host refuses to load it. The card displays a security warning: "This message cannot be verified. The sender's plugin signature is invalid." This is a hard E-stop.

---

## The Single Most Important Call
**Standardizing the Preview/Detail lifecycle transition.**

If you ship only one change next, remove the fixed `280dp` height and introduce the "Tap to Expand into Detail View" pattern. This single structural change forces you to define the `viewMode` in the plugin contract, solves the clipping problem for rich apps, and prevents simple notifications from taking up too much vertical space. It is the absolute bedrock of a usable micro-app feed.

## Things to Defer
1. **Plugin-Federated Global Search:** Do not attempt to let plugins hook into the *global* Inbox search bar yet. It requires complex timeout handling, ranking merging, and UI rendering handoffs across multiple isolated WebViews simultaneously. 
2. **Cross-Plugin Communication:** Do not let plugins talk to each other. The sandbox must remain completely isolated.
3. **Complex Inbox Folders:** Defer building UI for user-defined folders. Rely on the flat Inbox timeline + the secondary "Plugins" tab for now.

## Diverse Sender Needs
- **The Lottery Sender:** Needs a prominent Preview card showing "You won!" and a button. Doesn't need a Dashboard. Wants the card to auto-dismiss once the prize is claimed (benefits heavily from `dismissBehavior`).
- **The Trading Bot:** Needs a high-frequency feed. Benefits heavily from Inbox stacking (collapsing 5 price alerts into 1). Desperately needs the **App View** capability to render a full-screen portfolio chart using data cached in `platform.storage`.
- **The AI Agent (Human-in-the-loop):** Needs the Detail View. The prompt might be a long chat history context followed by an "Approve/Reject" action. The 280dp constraint makes reading chat history impossible; the Detail View allows a full-screen, scrollable log.

## SDK & Contract Changes Required

1. **Manifest Additions:**
   - `preferredPreviewHeight?: number;` (Hint to host in dp, capped by host).
   - `declaredCapabilities`: Expand the enum to include `APP_VIEW` and `SEARCH`.

2. **Platform Bridge Changes:**
   - **Environment Injection:** The host needs to inject context into the plugin on load so the plugin knows what to render. 
     `window.__syncler_env = { viewMode: 'preview' | 'detail' | 'app_view' };`
   - **Navigation Hook:** A way for a plugin in 'preview' mode to request expansion programmatically (e.g. if the user taps a specific button *inside* the webview instead of the host card background).
     `platform.ui.requestDetailView(): Promise<void>;`
   - **Lifecycle Hooks:**
     `__syncler_internal_dispatch('onSearch', [query: string])`

## Architectural Blockers
- **The WebView Leak:** The comment `// the bridge's CoroutineScope outlives the WebView` in `InboxScreen.kt` indicates a leak architecture. Moving to a Preview/Detail model means destroying and recreating WebViews constantly as the user scrolls the `LazyColumn` and expands cards. The WebView pooling and bridge cleanup must be bulletproof, or the app will rapidly crash with OOM errors.
- **State Loss on Re-render:** When a user taps a card to go from Preview to Detail, the host will likely destroy the Preview WebView and create a new Detail WebView. The plugin will lose all its DOM state. The SDK must heavily document that plugins must persist UI state in `platform.storage` or hydrate quickly purely from the `payloadJson`.

 succeeded in 286ms:
**Decision**

Keep: `title`, `subtitle`, `summary`, `searchText`.

Cut: `priority`, `category`, icon/color, preview timestamp, accessibility label.

```ts
// sdk-plugin
export interface HostPreview {
  /**
   * Required. Primary inbox row text.
   * Max 80 UTF-8 bytes after trimming.
   */
  title: string;

  /**
   * Optional. Secondary row text, usually sender-local context:
   * account, ticket, market, workflow, or short status.
   * Max 120 UTF-8 bytes.
   */
  subtitle?: string;

  /**
   * Optional. One compact human-readable sentence shown when the row has room.
   * Max 240 UTF-8 bytes.
   */
  summary?: string;

  /**
   * Optional. Extra normalized search terms for host-wide search.
   * Max 16 entries; each entry max 64 UTF-8 bytes.
   * The host indexes these in addition to title/subtitle/summary.
   */
  searchText?: string[];
}
```

```python
# sdk-python
from typing import TypedDict, NotRequired

class HostPreview(TypedDict):
    # Required. Primary inbox row text. Max 80 UTF-8 bytes after trimming.
    title: str

    # Optional. Secondary row text. Max 120 UTF-8 bytes.
    subtitle: NotRequired[str]

    # Optional. Compact preview sentence. Max 240 UTF-8 bytes.
    summary: NotRequired[str]

    # Optional. Extra host-search terms. Max 16 entries, 64 UTF-8 bytes each.
    searchText: NotRequired[list[str]]
```

**Yes/No Decisions**

- Required fields: **Yes**. Only `title` is required. Missing optional fields still render a sensible row.
- Field caps: **Yes**. `title` 80 bytes, `subtitle` 120, `summary` 240, `searchText` 16 x 64. Enough for dense inbox rows, bounded for polling.
- `searchText`: **Yes, array of tokens/phrases**. The sender knows domain terms best; the host indexes these plus visible text.
- Priority: **No**. Omitted. The host should not let senders silently influence row ordering or alarm styling.
- Category: **No**. Omitted. Too plugin-specific; use `subtitle` or `searchText`.
- Icon/color: **No**. Omitted. Visual identity comes from sender/plugin avatar and sender name.
- Timestamps: **No sender timestamp field**. Row displays server `sent_at`. If event time matters, put it in `subtitle` or `summary`.
- Accessibility label: **No**. Omitted. Host derives accessible text from sender name, sent time, title, subtitle, and summary.
- Missing `hostPreview`: **Yes fallback**. Host renders sender/plugin name as title, server `sent_at`, and generic text: `Encrypted message`.
- Payload size cap: **Yes**. Serialized `hostPreview` must be <= `1024` UTF-8 bytes. Larger previews are rejected or ignored.

**Rendered Examples**

Lottery card:

```json
{
  "title": "Lottery ticket entered",
  "subtitle": "Mega Millions - Ticket 8KQ-193",
  "summary": "5 lines entered for the May 22 drawing. Estimated jackpot: $120M.",
  "searchText": ["mega millions", "lottery", "ticket 8KQ-193", "may 22", "jackpot"]
}
```

Trading-bot price alert:

```json
{
  "title": "BTC crossed $71,500",
  "subtitle": "Momentum Bot - BTC/USD",
  "summary": "Price moved above your alert threshold with 2.4% 24h volume increase.",
  "searchText": ["btc", "bitcoin", "btcusd", "price alert", "71500", "momentum bot"]
}
```

 succeeded in 286ms:
This contract defines the structured metadata embedded in the encrypted payload under the reserved `hostPreview` key. This allows the host application to render inbox rows natively without waking up the plugin.

### 1. TypeScript interface (`sdk-plugin`)

```ts
/**
 * Structured metadata used by the host to render inbox rows natively.
 * Embedded in the encrypted message payload under the `hostPreview` key.
 */
export interface HostPreview {
  /** Main bold text for the inbox row. Required. Max 64 chars. */
  title: string;
  /** Secondary text shown below the title. Max 128 chars. */
  subtitle?: string;
  /** Brief snippet for expanded views or notifications. Max 256 chars. */
  summary?: string;
  /** Hints for sorting or highlighting. Defaults to 'normal'. */
  priority?: 'low' | 'normal' | 'high' | 'urgent';
  /** 
   * Keywords for the host's global search index. 
   * Max 10 tokens, 32 chars each.
   */
  searchText?: string[];
  /** 
   * Optional ISO-8601 timestamp to override the display time. 
   * Useful for historical data or event-specific alerts.
   */
  timestamp?: string;
  /** 
   * Custom screen-reader label. 
   * Falls back to "[title], [subtitle]" if absent. 
   */
  accessibilityLabel?: string;
}
```

### 2. Python `TypedDict` (`sdk-python`)

```python
from typing import TypedDict, List, Literal, Optional

class HostPreview(TypedDict, total=False):
    """
    Structured metadata for native host rendering.
    
    The sender passes this inside the payload dict to client.send_to().
    Example: client.send_to(..., payload={"hostPreview": {...}, "data": ...})
    """
    title: str               # Required (semantic), max 64 chars
    subtitle: str            # Optional, max 128 chars
    summary: str             # Optional, max 256 chars
    priority: Literal["low", "normal", "high", "urgent"]
    searchText: List[str]    # Max 10 tokens, 32 chars each
    timestamp: str           # ISO-8601 format string
    accessibilityLabel: str  # Screen reader override
```

### 3. Rendered Examples

#### Lottery Card (Normal Priority)
```json
{
  "hostPreview": {
    "title": "Weekly Mega Jackpot",
    "subtitle": "$12,000,000 Drawing Tonight",
    "summary": "Your numbers: 04-12-29-33-41. Drawing at 9 PM EST.",
    "priority": "normal",
    "searchText": ["lottery", "jackpot", "weekly"]
  },
  "draw_id": "8823-abc",
  "numbers": [4, 12, 29, 33, 41]
}
```

#### Trading-bot Price Alert (High Priority)
```json
{
  "hostPreview": {
    "title": "BTC/USD Alert: $65,000",
    "subtitle": "Price target reached (Up 5.2%)",
    "summary": "RSI at 72. Moving averages cross detected on 1H chart.",
    "priority": "high",
    "searchText": ["trading", "btc", "crypto", "alert"],
    "timestamp": "2026-05-21T14:30:00Z"
  },
  "symbol": "BTC/USD",
  "price": 65000.42,
  "indicators": {"rsi": 72, "ma_cross": true}
}
```

### Constraints & Justification

*   **Required vs optional**: `title` is the only mandatory field. A row must have at least one identifying string.
*   **Field length caps**: 64/128/256 chars. These limits ensure the metadata fits mobile layouts and keeps the decryption/parsing overhead predictable.
*   **`searchText`**: `string[]` (tokens). Providing tokens directly allows the host to build a simple prefix-index or set for global search without complex parsing.
*   **Priority**: Enum (`low`, `normal`, `high`, `urgent`). Allows the host to pin urgent alerts or mute low-priority noise.
*   **Category**: **Omitted**. Plugin-level filtering is sufficient; per-message categorization is redundant for a 2-line inbox row.
*   **Icon / color**: **Omitted**. Brand identity is derived from the sender's verified name and avatar.
*   **Timestamps**: `timestamp` (optional ISO string). Enables accurate "at a glance" timing for historical imports or delayed alerts.
*   **Accessibility**: `accessibilityLabel` provides a flat string for screen readers, preventing "jumbled" reading of nested metadata.
*   **Fallback**: If `hostPreview` is missing (legacy sender), the host renders: "New message from [Sender Name]".
*   **Payload size cap**: **2KB**. The total `hostPreview` object must not exceed 2048 bytes to ensure fast inbox processing during message polling.

**Findings**

- **High: state is not cleared or account-scoped on logout.**  
  [UserStateRepository.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepository.kt:58) loads one singleton encrypted-pref blob, while logout only clears `Session` in [Session.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/auth/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/auth/Session.kt:57). A different user logging in during the same app install can inherit the previous userג€™s local read/plugin state; if the new userג€™s remote state is empty, `pull()` merges old local state into that account and a later `push()` can upload it encrypted under the new userג€™s key. Fix by clearing `UserStateRepository` on logout or keying local state by user id.

- **High: local mutations can lose read/archive entries.**  
  `markRead()` and `markArchived()` do `_state.value` read, transform, then `applyLocal()` outside any mutex in [UserStateRepository.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/UserStateRepository.kt:74). Two concurrent marks can both read the same base state and the later assignment wins. There is also a pull race: `pull()` can merge/apply remote state while `markRead()` is holding a stale computed copy, and the later `applyLocal()` can overwrite the pull merge. Use a serialized local mutation path, or atomic `update {}` plus serialized disk persistence and merge application.

- **High: failed pushes are not actually retried on foreground.**  
  The log says failed mark-read push ג€will retryג€, and CAS retry failure says ג€will retry laterג€, but only `markRead()`/`markArchived()` call `push()`. `InboxViewModel` init and refresh only call `pull()` in [InboxScreen.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxScreen.kt:88). A read mark whose push fails can remain local forever unless another local mutation happens. Add a dirty flag/outbox and flush on unlock/foreground after pull.

- **Medium: timestamp string comparison does not reliably implement `max(read_at)`.**  
  [StateMerger.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/storage/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/storage/StateMerger.kt:51) compares ISO strings directly. `Instant.toString()` may emit `...00Z` or `...00.500Z`; lexicographically, `...00Z` sorts after `...00.500Z`, even though it is earlier. Compare parsed `Instant`s or serialize fixed-width timestamps. This also affects archive merge at line 57.

- **Medium: future schema handling can silently corrupt unknown fields.**  
  `fromJson()` preserves unknown `schema_version` values in [EncryptedUserState.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/storage/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/storage/EncryptedUserState.kt:65), but `toJson()` only writes known fields. A V2 client reading V3 will drop V3-only fields while still writing `schema_version: 3`. Unknown future schema should either be preserved as raw JSON or treated as read-only / non-pushable.

**Answers To The Review Points**

The V1 migration test is useful but not enough. Add a full V1 compatibility test with `installed_plugins`, `dismissed_messages`, `plugin_settings`, and `user_scoped_storage` round-tripping through `fromJson()->toJson()->fromJson`. An unknown V3 test is also worthwhile, but it should assert your policy: preserve unknowns or refuse to write, not merely ג€doesnג€™t crashג€.

Same-timestamp read tiebreaker is fine for now because `ReadMessageEntry` has no device id, so the bias is unobservable. If you add device metadata later, add a deterministic tiebreaker.

One CAS retry is acceptable only with a real dirty retry path. Right now the server CAS defects from review #31 appear fixed, and Android doesnג€™t depend on parsing the 409 body, but the client has no durable retry scheduling.

Encryption format looks compatible: [Aead.encrypt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/crypto/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/crypto/MasterKey.kt:29) returns `nonce + ciphertext`, matching [docs/crypto-spec.md](D:/Projects/syncler/docs/crypto-spec.md:53). Server stores the state blob opaquely.

The Phase 2 implementation of read-state sync introduces critical concurrency and multi-user safety issues in `UserStateRepository.kt`. While the schema migration and UI visual treatment are sound, the core synchronization logic risks data loss and cross-user contamination.

### 1. Schema & Merge Semantics

*   **Forward Migration:** `EncryptedUserState.fromJson` correctly handles V0/V1 blobs by defaulting `readMessages` and `archivedMessages` to empty lists. This is non-destructive for existing V1 fields.
*   **Forward Compatibility Risk:** As noted in the prompt, a V2 client encountering a V3 blob (from a future client) will parse only known fields and drop V3-specific data on the next `toJson -> push` cycle. While we "own all clients," preserving unknown fields in `EncryptedUserState` (e.g., via a `Map<String, Any?>` for unrecognized JSON keys) would be a more robust "lesson learned" from M7.
*   **Merge Determinism:** `StateMerger` uses `a.readAt >= b.readAt` where `a` is local and `b` is remote. This correctly implements "local wins on equality," providing a deterministic tie-breaker for identical timestamps.

### 2. UserStateRepository: Concurrency & Atomicity (CRITICAL)

The current implementation has several race conditions that will lead to lost updates in production:

*   **Non-Atomic Local Mutation:** `markRead` (and `markArchived`) reads `_state.value`, copies it, and writes back. If two messages are marked read simultaneously, one will overwrite the other, losing the first update.
    *   *Fix:* Use `_state.update { ... }` (available on `MutableStateFlow`) or gate mutations with `syncMutex`.
*   **Pull vs. MarkRead Race:** `pull()` fetches remote state and merges it with the *current* `_state.value`. If a user marks a message read *during* the network call, `pull()`'s final `applyLocal()` will overwrite that new local mark with the stale merge result.
    *   *Fix:* The read-merge-write cycle in `pull` must be atomic relative to local mutations.
*   **Concurrent Pushes:** While `push()` is gated by `syncMutex`, multiple `markRead` calls will queue multiple `push()` operations. If the first push succeeds, the second push will re-encrypt and re-push the exact same state (redundant but safe). If the first fails with 409, the conflict handler runs, but the second queued push will still trigger.

### 3. Multi-User Safety & Logout (CRITICAL)

`UserStateRepository` is a `@Singleton` and does not clear its state on logout.
*   **Cross-User Contamination:** If User A logs out and User B logs in on the same device, `UserStateRepository` still holds User A's `readMessages` in memory (and on disk in `EncryptedSharedPreferences`).
*   **Data Corruption:** When User B triggers a `pull()`, the repository merges User B's remote state with User A's stale local state. User B now "inherits" User A's read marks and installed plugins. On the next `push()`, this corrupted state is written to User B's server account.
*   **Privacy Leak:** Even before a `pull`, the UI will show User A's read marks to User B.
    *   *Fix:* `UserStateRepository` must expose a `clear()` method called by `AuthRepository.logout()`, or be scoped to the session.

### 4. UI & Visuals

*   **Layout Stability:** Preserving the 8dp dot slot when read is the correct choice to prevent horizontal jitter when the user marks a row read.
*   **Trigger Logic:** Marking read on "detail open" is consistent with the conservative "scanning is not reading" philosophy.
*   **Logout/Login Lifecycle:** The `initialValue` in `InboxViewModel.readMessageIds` correctly pulls from the repository's current state, but as noted above, that state might be stale/stolen from a previous user if the app wasn't process-killed between sessions.

### 5. Sync Correctness

*   **CAS Policy:** One retry in `handleConflictAndRetry` is a pragmatic V1 policy. If a second 409 occurs, bailing and waiting for the next foreground/poll tick prevents infinite loops.
*   **Encryption Format:** The use of `Aead.encrypt` (nonce || ciphertext+tag) matches the project's standard for message-body encryption and is appropriate for the opaque server blob.

### Recommendations

1.  **Immediate Fix:** Add a `clear()` method to `UserStateRepository` that resets `_state` and clears `SharedPreferences`. Call it in `AuthRepository.logout()`.
2.  **Atomicity:** Refactor `markRead`, `markArchived`, and `pull` to use a consistent locking strategy (or `update {}` for the Flow) to ensure the read-modify-write cycle is atomic.
3.  **Future-Proofing:** Consider updating `EncryptedUserState` to retain unknown JSON fields to prevent data loss when mixing client versions.

# Review 37 ג€” Phase 1: hostPreview contract + preview/detail split

Implementation follows the contract for the most part, but there is one **critical omission** in the Android validator (Total Cap) and a documentation hazard in the integration guide.

## Contract enforcement

### 1. Byte-cap parity
- **Status:** **Partial.**
- **Mismatch:** The 2048-byte **total cap** is missing in the Android implementation.
    - `sdk-python` (L88) and `sdk-plugin` (L128) both serialize the block to JSON and verify it stays under 2048 bytes.
    - `Android: InboxRepository.kt::parseHostPreview` (L223) checks individual fields (80/120/240/64) but never checks the total size of the block. A sender could bypass the 2KB limit by including many large unknown extension fields or a maxed-out `searchText` array that, combined with other fields, exceeds 2KB.
- **Minor Inconsistency:** `searchText` empty tokens.
    - Android (L255) rejects the entire block if any token in `searchText` is `isEmpty()`.
    - SDKs allow empty strings (they only cap the max bytes). This is a safe deviation but technically a contract mismatch.

### 2. Side-effects of fallback
- **Status:** **Verified.**
- `InboxRepository.kt::parseHostPreview` is wrapped in `runCatching` (L223) and returns `null` on any violation.
- `InboxRow` (L146) correctly switches to the generic "New message from {senderName}" template when `preview == null`.
- The plugin still loads the full `payloadJson` in the detail view; the malformed `hostPreview` block is simply ignored by the host but preserved for the plugin.

### 3. Total-cap test
- **Finding:** The documented fields alone sum to 1,512 bytes (80+120+240 + 16*64 + JSON overhead). The ~500B headroom for "unknown fields" is a sound design choice for future-proofing, but **must be enforced on the host** to prevent payload bloat in the inbox database.

## Preview/detail split

### 4. WebView lifecycle
- **Status:** **Clean.**
- `InboxScreen.kt::PluginRenderView` uses `onRelease` (L237) to call `bridge.destroy()`, `removeJavascriptInterface`, and `webView.destroy()`.
- Since `DetailScreen` is conditionally composed based on `selectedId` (L97), setting `selectedId = null` (back action) removes the entire sub-tree, triggering `onRelease`.
- Fast back/open cycles are safe because each `AndroidView` gets a fresh `WebView` instance.

### 5. `selectedId` vs `items` race
- **Status:** **Correct.**
- If a background poll-refresh removes the selected item (e.g. it expired), `selectedItem` (L96) becomes null on the next recomposition, and the UI correctly flips back to the list view.
- Note: The current `InboxRepository.refresh` (L77) only appends/merges; it doesn't seem to prune expired items yet, so this race won't trigger in practice until Phase 4 (Cleanup).

### 6. No mark-read
- **Status:** **Fine.** Deferring visual unread states to Phase 2 (M7) is appropriate given the scope of the preview/detail split.

## Fallback / failure paths

### 7. UI affordance for malformed metadata
- **Finding:** Currently, there is no visual indicator that a message *intended* to have a preview but failed validation. 
- **Recommendation:** Stick with the current "silent fallback." Surfacing "Malformed Metadata" errors to end-users is alarmist. If a sender is broken, they'll see the failure in their own SDK logs/tests during development (ֲ§9 of the guide).

### 8. Bundle not yet fetched
- **Status:** **Correct.**
- `DetailScreen` (L186) shows a "Plugin not loaded" card with the raw `PayloadFallbackView` if `bundleJs` is null.
- This is better than hiding the row, as it allows the user to see the encrypted content (best effort) even if the CDN is down or the hash check failed.

## Doc consistency

### 9. Documentation Chain
- **Status:** **Consistent.** `integration-guide.md` ֲ§2 table matches the SDK/Host byte limits (except for the missing Android total-cap enforcement mentioned above).

### 10. ֲ§3 Example Hazard
- **Status:** **Conflicting.**
- `integration-guide.md` ֲ§3 example code shows `onMessage` calling `platform.showNotification`.
- However, the text immediately below and the implementation in `RenderShell.kt` (L93) explicitly **reject** `showNotification` in V1 inbox mode.
- **Fix:** Revise the ֲ§3 example to remove `onMessage` or have it `console.log`. Using a forbidden API in the primary "Getting Started" example is a high-friction footgun for integrators.

## Summary of Fixes Required

1. **Android:** Add `totalMaxBytes` (2048) check to `InboxRepository.kt::parseHostPreview`.
2. **Docs:** Update `integration-guide.md` ֲ§3 to remove the `showNotification` call from the example code.
