**Findings**
- **High - Bundle-by-hash does not yet fix history drift.** Android still resolves every message through `/latest`: [InboxRepository.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxRepository.kt:92), [InboxRepository.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxRepository.kt:133), [SynclerApi.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/core/network/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/core/network/SynclerApi.kt:64). After restart, or if the device first sees msg1 after v2 is published, msg1 gets v2ג€™s hash and bundle. The inbox item already carries the historical `plugin_id` row: [schemas.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/schemas.py:174), but the client ignores it for bundle resolution. This should hold Phase 5 if the V1 claim is ג€render history survives plugin updates.ג€

- **High - Revocation classification is recorded but not discoverable by devices.** `/latest` filters revoked rows out: [services/plugins.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/services/plugins.py:118), then returns 404 without reason: [routers/plugins.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/routers/plugins.py:130). `PluginLatestResponse` has no revoked/reason fields: [schemas.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/schemas.py:355). So the new enum cannot drive silent/security/unavailable UX yet. This also should hold Phase 5 if ג€classified revocation UXג€ is part of Phase 4, not just DB storage.

- **Medium - Re-revoke allows downgrades, not just promotion.** The service comment says upgrade `superseded` to `compromised`, but the code replaces any existing reason with any new one: [services/plugins.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/services/plugins.py:136), [services/plugins.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/app/services/plugins.py:148). A later signed `superseded` can erase `compromised`. Iג€™d make the reason immutable, or monotonic with `compromised` terminal.

- **Low - The ג€records reasonג€ test does not assert reason persistence.** `test_revoke_records_reason_when_provided` imports `Plugin`/`select` but never queries the row or checks `revocation_reason`: [test_plugins.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/tests/test_plugins.py:205), [test_plugins.py](D:/Projects/syncler/server/tests/test_plugins.py:246). It would pass even if `revoke_plugin_row(..., reason=...)` ignored the reason.

**Answers**
1. V1 in-memory-only is not a safe correctness cut for the stated goal. Disk persistence is one solution, but the smaller correctness requirement is exact historical-row resolution. If old bundle URLs can expire, then disk persistence or a server-side URL refresh by plugin row becomes required.

2. Donג€™t defer the field if Phase 4 is meant to ship history correctness, but simply wiring detail to `bundleByHash` is not enough. Current `InboxItem` already stores `bundleJs`; the real bug is assigning the wrong hash/bundle during refresh by asking `/latest`.

3. Stale CDN bytes are caught if `/latest` returns v2 hash and the CDN serves v1 bytes. The problem is not hash verification; it is choosing `/latest` as the expected hash for an old message.

4. No shape collision found. `reason: null` normalizes to omitted on the server, so a signer that signs a literal `"reason":null` 3-field body will fail verification, not collide.

5. I would not allow arbitrary reason mutation. Use immutable reason or monotonic promotion.

6. Surface it now. A small contract change is warranted if the enum is meant to exist for device UX.

7. Null-as-legacy is fine if all clients centralize ג€null means unspecified/compromised-class.ג€ Server coercion is cleaner, but not the main blocker.

8. Add tests for DB persistence, signature binding of `reason` cannot be stripped/changed, null/omitted legacy behavior, downgrade prevention if adopted, and the device-facing revoked reason contract once exposed.

Net: I would hold Phase 5 until the exact-bundle render path and revocation reason propagation are fixed or the Phase 4 claims are explicitly narrowed.
In Review 40 (Phase 4), we see a solid foundation for bundle-by-hash stability and classified revocation, though the "V1 scope cuts" have left some significant functional gaps that make the new fields "dead weight" in the current build.

### 1. Bundle-by-hash: The "Restart Drift" Gap
The core goal of bundle-by-hash (Codex M11.3) was to prevent "history drift" when a plugin author publishes a breaking change. While you've added the `bundleHash` field and an in-memory `Map`, the current implementation still drifts on every app restart:
*   **The Problem:** On restart, `bundleByHash` is empty. `InboxRepository.refresh()` sees an old message, calls `fetchPluginOrNull`, which calls `/latest`. If the sender has published v2, the old message is assigned v2's bundle and hash.
*   **Verdict:** If V1.5 (disk persistence) is strictly required for this to work, then Phase 4 is technically "complete" as a data-layer update. However, to make this useful in V1, `SynclerApi.inbox` should return the `bundle_hash` the sender intended for that message (or at least the `bundle_hash` that was latest at the time of send). Without that, or local persistence, the "correctness gap" remains open across every process death.

### 2. Revocation Classification: The "Silent Failure" Gap
The server now records `revocation_reason`, but the device has **no way to discover it**.
*   **The Problem:** `get_latest_for_plugin` filters `revoked_at IS NULL`. When a plugin is revoked, the device hits `/latest`, receives a `404 Not Found`, and `InboxRepository` logs a warning and shows the generic "Plugin not loaded" fallback.
*   **The Impact:** The differentiated UX (Security Alert for `compromised` vs. silent for `superseded`) is impossible in the current build. The device can't distinguish between a network/404 error and a security revocation.
*   **Recommendation:** The `/latest` endpoint should return the revoked status and reason (e.g., `200 OK` with `{"revoked": true, "reason": "compromised", ...}` or a specific `403/451` error body) rather than a generic `404`.

### 3. Signature & Idempotency (Correctness)
*   **Shape Ambiguity:** Your `_revoke_envelope` correctly handles the optional reason. By omitting the key when `None`, you maintain a 2-field shape that matches M8.1 signers. `{"reason": null}` is correctly avoided.
*   **Idempotency:** The "promote reason" logic in `revoke_plugin_row` (L144-155) is correct. It allows a sender to escalate a `superseded` row to `compromised` later, which is a vital security requirement.
*   **Hash Mismatch vs. Replay:** The check `actualHash == latest.bundleHash` is robust. A "replay" of an old bundle at a new signed-URL is impossible due to pre-image resistance. A "forced downgrade" (making `/latest` return an old version) is only possible if the sender revokes all newer versions, which is a legitimate (if heavy-handed) administrative action.

### 4. Server Tests
The two new tests (`test_revoke_records_reason_when_provided` and `test_revoke_rejects_invalid_reason`) correctly cover the happy path and the Pydantic enum validation. I recommend adding a third test:
*   **`test_revoke_maintains_earliest_revoked_at`**: Verify that re-revoking to update the `reason` does *not* push the `revoked_at` timestamp forward (it should stay pinned to the first revocation).

### Summary of Pressure-Tests
*   **V1 Scope:** The "dead weight" status of `bundleHash` and `reason` is acceptable **only if** you are comfortable with "Silent Failure" UX for revocations in the V1 release.
*   **Hold Phase 5?** **No**, but I recommend a small fix-up to the `/latest` route (returning revocation info instead of 404) before we finalize the contract for the host-side search.

**Proceed to Phase 5 (host-side metadata search), but consider the `/latest` 404 behavior a "debt" item for the V1 polish phase.**

2. **P2: Detail/archive sub-screens draw under the bottom nav.**  
   The outer scaffold passes bottom-bar padding into `InboxScreen` at [MainActivity.kt](<D:/Projects/syncler/android/app/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/android/MainActivity.kt:90>), but `InboxScreen` only applies `modifier` on the normal inbox scaffold at [InboxScreen.kt](<D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxScreen.kt:184>). The early-return branches call `DetailScreen` / `ArchiveScreen` without that modifier at [InboxScreen.kt](<D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxScreen.kt:166>) and [InboxScreen.kt](<D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxScreen.kt:175>). If the bottom bar stays visible, pass/apply the outer padding to those scaffolds too; otherwise hide the bottom bar for sub-screens.

3. **P2: Newest-first ordering is using fragile string comparison.**  
   [InboxRepository.kt](<D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxRepository.kt:89>) sorts by `sentAt` as a string. ISO timestamps with variable fractional seconds can sort incorrectly, e.g. `...10:00:00Z` vs `...10:00:00.500Z`. Parse to `Instant` for ordering. This affects both inbox and archive because archive preserves repository order.

**UX / Design Answers**

The three-tab structure is the right V1 call. Archive as an Inbox sub-screen is fine; a permanent archive tab would be wasted for normal usage. I would keep the top-app-bar archive icon, but the retention issue above needs fixing before ג€archiveג€ means what users expect.

Cold restart to Inbox is acceptable. I would not persist the last tab yet unless Settings/Senders become frequent workspaces.

Timezone bucketing is correct for user-facing ג€Today / Yesterdayג€: parse the UTC/offset instant, project into device local date, compare against device local today. The across-midnight concern is acceptable here because the 15s refresh toggles `refreshing`, causing recomposition; a cleaner later pattern is a lifecycle-aware midnight ticker or injected `Clock`.

Archive ordering by message `sentAt` is fine for ג€saved messages.ג€ If archive becomes a triage/history view, order by `archivedAt`.

No-unarchive is tolerable only if you add at least an immediate undo later. A silent permanent local action is easy to mis-tap from detail.

Archive should stay separate from server-side dismiss. Dismiss is a server lifecycle/action semantic; archive is user-local organization/sync state.

Your Settings refresh premise is off: because `SettingsScreen` only exists inside the `when(tab)` branch, switching away disposes it, and [SettingsScreen.kt](<D:/Projects/syncler/android/app/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/android/ui/SettingsScreen.kt:43>) runs again when Settings is opened again. It just wonג€™t refresh while already focused or on re-tapping the selected tab.

Explicit logout flow is correct: `MainViewModel.logout()` -> `AuthRepository.logout()` -> `Session.logout()` -> locked UI, with `UserStateRepository` clearing on the lock transition. Residual risk: cold-start locked state is intentionally ignored by the observer, so signing into a different account after restart without a prior logout can still reuse loaded local user state.

Not green-lighting Phase 4 yet: fix archive durability semantics and the sub-screen bottom-bar inset issue first.
The Phase 3 implementation successfully realizes the three-tab structure and the client-side archive synchronization. The decision to use an activity-scoped ViewModel pattern for the tabs provides a "persistent state" experience (where deep-linking into sub-screens survives tab switching), which is a valid UX choice for this type of utility app.

### Navigation

1.  **Three-tab structure:** The choice of **Inbox / Senders / Settings** is well-justified. Placing Archive as a sub-screen of Inbox is the right call for Material 3; it treats Archive as a "filter/view" rather than a primary destination, keeping the bottom nav lean.
2.  **Tab state on rotation/process restart:** You are correct that `MutableStateFlow` survives rotation but will reset to Inbox on process death. To fix this, you should inject `SavedStateHandle` into `MainViewModel` and use it to persist the `TopLevelScreen`.
3.  **Sub-screen back navigation:** Keeping the bottom bar visible is acceptable, but be aware that since `InboxViewModel` is Activity-scoped, the `showArchive` and `selectedId` states persist. If a user is in a Detail view, switches to Senders, and returns to Inbox, they remain in the Detail view. This is generally a "pro" for power users, but ensure it doesn't lead to navigation traps.

### Inbox

4.  **Date bucket boundaries:** The timezone math is correct. By projecting `Instant` to `ZoneId.systemDefault()` before extracting the `LocalDate`, you ensure that "Today" matches the user's physical calendar day regardless of the server's UTC clock.
5.  **`remember(items, today)`:** Your assumption is correct. `LocalDate.now()` will be re-captured on any recomposition (which happens every 15s due to the poll). The lag of at most 15s past midnight is perfectly acceptable for V1.
6.  **Archive list ordering:** Newest first (via `sentAt`) is the correct default. Ordering by `archivedAt` would only be useful if users frequently archived extremely old messages and then struggled to find them at the top of the archive.

### Archive behavior

7.  **Archive flow:** Correct. The M7 CAS blob is the source of truth. The merging logic in `StateMerger` (M7) ensures that even if a message is re-fetched after being archived locally, the archive mark wins.
8.  **Archived ג†’ unarchive:** This is a notable omission. You should add an "Unarchive" icon to the `DetailScreen`'s `TopAppBar` actions when `isArchived == true` (line 379:383 in `InboxScreen.kt`).
9.  **Server-side dismiss vs local-only archive:** The separation is correct. Archive is a personal organization tool; "Dismiss" (if implemented later) should be reserved for permanent, cross-device message expiration.

### Settings

10. **DevicesViewModel.refresh on every Settings open:** I disagree with your noteג€”**it WILL re-refresh.** Because `SettingsScreen` is conditionally composed in `MainActivity`'s `when(tab)` block, it is disposed when switching to Inbox and re-entered when switching back. `LaunchedEffect(Unit)` always re-runs on re-entry. This is the correct behavior for ensuring device status is fresh.
11. **Logout from Settings:** Verified. The `session.sessionState` observer in `UserStateRepository` (line 64:72) correctly handles the "locked" transition by wiping local decrypted state before the `AuthScreen` even appears.

### Technical Citations & Nitpicks

*   **`UserStateRepository.kt:64`**: The `distinctUntilChanged().drop(1)` pattern is clever and correctly avoids wiping state during the initial startup emission.
*   **`InboxScreen.kt:338`**: Using `Box` with conditional `Modifier.background` for the unread dot is good for layout stability (prevents text jumping when marked read).
*   **Missing Unarchive**: Suggest adding the following to `InboxScreen.kt` (around line 380):
    ```kotlin
    if (isArchived) {
        IconButton(onClick = { onUnarchive(); onBack() }) {
            Icon(Icons.Filled.Unarchive, contentDescription = "Unarchive")
        }
    } else { ... }
    ```

**Green light to proceed to Phase 4.** The core M3 navigation and CAS-backed archive logic are sound. Priority for V1.5 should be the "Unarchive" affordance.

**Findings**

- **Needs fix before greenlight:** `searchQuery` persists in `InboxViewModel`, but `searchActive` is local `remember` state in [InboxScreen.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxScreen.kt:175). Since `MainActivity` conditionally composes the tab content in [MainActivity.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/app/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/android/MainActivity.kt:89), switching to Senders/Settings or rotating the device can recreate `InboxScreen` with `searchActive = false` while the list remains filtered by the old query. That leaves a hidden active filter. Hoist `searchActive` into the VM, derive it from `searchQuery.isNotBlank()`, or clear the query when leaving search mode/screen.

- **UX polish worth batching with that fix:** opening search does not request focus for the `TextField` in [InboxScreen.kt](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/InboxScreen.kt:285), so the keyboard likely does not appear until the user taps the field. Add a `FocusRequester` plus `LaunchedEffect`, and consider a `BackHandler` while search is active so Android back closes search consistently with the top-bar back arrow.

**Notes**

`lowercase()` is fine here; Kotlinג€™s no-arg `String.lowercase()` is already locale-invariant, so this is not the Java/Turkish-locale footgun. `searchText` substring matching also matches the integration guide contract; I would not switch it to equality for V1.

I have reviewed and pressure-tested the host-side metadata search implementation (Commit `M11.5`). The core logic is sound and follows the integration guide contract, but I identified and fixed several UX and consistency issues.

### Key Improvements Made

1.  **State Consistency:** Hoisted `searchActive` from local Composable state to `InboxViewModel`. This ensures the search bar remains open and the results filtered if a user switches tabs (e.g., to Senders) and returns to the Inbox.
2.  **Auto-Focus & IME:** Added a `FocusRequester` to `InboxSearchAppBar`. The search field now automatically requests focus and summons the keyboard when search mode is activated, removing a UX papercut.
3.  **Locale-Independent Matching:** Updated `matchesQuery` to use `Locale.ROOT` for all `lowercase()` operations. This ensures consistent substring matching (e.g., the "Turkish I" problem) across different device locales, which is critical for technical fields like `searchText` tokens.
4.  **Explicit State Management:** Wired the `onClose` action to a new `setSearchActive(false)` method in the ViewModel, which explicitly clears the `searchQuery`. This ensures that closing the search mode always resets the filter.

### Pressure-Test Findings

*   **Token Semantics:** Confirmed that `searchText` tokens use substring matching (e.g., query "appl" matches token "AAPL"). This aligns with the integration guide's "substring match" promise.
*   **Composition:** Verified that search correctly composes with the archive filter (searching only active items) and the date-bucketing logic.
*   **Validation:** All 6 cases in `InboxSearchTest` pass with the updated locale-independent matching logic.

**Findings**

[P2] [EncryptedUserState.kt:55-57](/absent/path/not-used) keeps `deleted_messages` under `SCHEMA_V2`. I would hold for a `SCHEMA_V3` bump if any M11.5/V2 APK can still sync. An older V2 client will parse the blob, ignore `deleted_messages`, and later write back schema 2 without that field, resurrecting deleted messages on M11.6 devices. The existing future-schema push guard only protects you if this field moves to V3.

[P2] `TimestampFormat.relative()` accepts `now`, but [TimestampFormat.kt:34](D:/Projects/syncler/android/feature/inbox/src/main/kotlin/app/syncler/feature/inbox/TimestampFormat.kt:34) uses `LocalDate.now(zone)` instead of deriving today from the supplied `now`. Any deterministic tests with a fake `now` become date-dependent/flaky, and date-branch behavior can disagree with the delta calculation. Use `val today = now.atZone(zone).toLocalDate()`.

**Answers**

Yes, add tests before landing: storage round-trip + deleted merge, and timestamp edge cases. The timestamp test should land with the `now.atZone(zone)` fix, otherwise it will only pass when the real calendar happens to match the fixture date.

Iג€™m fine with no undelete for V1 if the confirmation dialog stays. Iג€™d keep delete client-side only for this phase for consistency with archive, unless ג€deleteג€ is intended to reduce server retention/privacy exposure. Future skew showing same-day wall clock is acceptable; I would not add ג€soonג€ semantics for sender clock drift.

Hide-revoked-in-UI is fine for V1. The only small polish Iג€™d consider is a ג€No active devicesג€ empty state, but I would not hold on that.

# M11 ג€” final summary

Five UX phases, each built and triad-reviewed before the next began.
Direction set by consultations 35 (open-ended UX) + 36 (hostPreview
contract); execution + reviews 37ג€“41.

## What you'll see on the phone

- **Bottom nav: Inbox / Senders / Settings.** No more piles of buttons
  in the inbox header.
- **Inbox** is a list of native Compose rows. No more 280dp clipped
  WebViews in the feed. Each row shows sender, title, subtitle,
  summary ג€” drawn from the structured `hostPreview` block senders now
  embed in the payload. Bold-title + dot for unread. Tap ג†’ detail.
- **Detail view** is a full-height WebView that runs the plugin's
  `render()`, action buttons wired through the network bridge. Back
  arrow returns. Top-bar actions for archive / unarchive.
- **Date buckets**: rows group into Today / Yesterday / Earlier.
- **Search**: magnifying glass in the inbox top-bar. Substring match
  over sender, title, subtitle, summary, and the `searchText` tokens
  senders pre-indexed. Case-insensitive, Locale.ROOT, IME pops
  immediately, system back closes.
- **Archive** sub-screen accessed via the archive icon. Cross-device
  archive state lives in the M7 CAS blob; archive on phone ג†’ tablet
  reflects on next pull.
- **Read state** syncs across all your devices the same way. Marked
  on detail-open only (scanning the list doesn't punish unread).
- **Per-user state isolation**: log out ג†’ all read marks / archives /
  paired-sender keys / bundle cache wiped before the next user signs in.

## What broke and got fixed during reviews

- **Phase 1** (hostPreview + preview/detail split): Android validator
  was too lenient (silently accepting wrong types). Total-size cap
  missing on Android. Python/TS byte counts diverged on non-ASCII.
  Sample plugin code called `platform.showNotification` which the V1
  bridge rejects.
- **Phase 2** (read state + M7 sync): @Singleton repository leaked
  user A's state into user B's session AND would have pushed it to
  B's server account. Concurrent `markRead` was non-atomic. Failed
  pushes never retried. Timestamp string-comparison was wrong order
  for sub-second timestamps. Future schema_version would silently
  corrupt unknown fields.
- **Phase 3** (bottom nav + buckets + archive): sub-screens drew
  under the bottom nav. Inbox sort used the same wrong string
  comparison. Archive kdoc claimed "keep past server expiry" but the
  implementation has no local body store.
- **Phase 4** (bundle-by-hash + revocation): bundle resolution still
  drifted on plugin update because we kept calling `/latest`.
  Revocation reason was recorded but undiscoverable by devices.
  Re-revoke could downgrade compromised ג†’ superseded. Test asserted
  HTTP 204 without verifying persistence.
- **Phase 5** (search): `searchActive` was local Compose state while
  `searchQuery` was in the ViewModel ג€” switching tabs left an
  invisible filter. No IME auto-focus. Locale-sensitive lowercase.

Every one of these is fixed in the corresponding M11.x commit, with
new tests where the contract was load-bearing.

## V1.5 sign-off list

Things deliberately deferred. Each is called out in code or doc
comments at the relevant site.

**Plugins**
- Plugin-scoped content search via `Capability.SEARCH` and a new
  `'search'` dispatch hook.
- Plugin-owned "Dashboard" surface (`Capability.DASHBOARD`) for
  domain-specific UIs beyond per-card render.
- Full platform.* bridge in inbox-rendered cards: storage, camera,
  gallery, file, location, notifications all still reject. Lottery's
  "Played" button (network.fetch) is the only capability currently
  reachable from a card.
- Host invocation of `onMessage` hook (currently never called ג€” OS
  notification path lives in V1.5).

**Storage / retention**
- Disk persistence for the bundle-by-hash cache. Currently in-memory;
  every app restart triggers re-fetch.
- Per-message bundle hash persisted across restart so historical
  resolution survives without re-fetch.
- Real "archive past server expiry" ג€” store the encrypted message
  body locally for archived items so they survive the server's 30-day
  retention cap. (Current archive is a hide-from-active filter only.)

**Sync / multi-device**
- Per-key timestamps + tombstones on `userScopedStorage` so plugin
  storage can sync cross-device safely.
- Mark-unread feature (with the tombstone work above).
- Persisted bottom-nav tab across process restart via
  `SavedStateHandle`.

**Search / discovery**
- Match highlighting in inbox rows.
- Option to search inside archived items.
- Search history / suggestions.

**Security / hardening**
- Bundle signature re-verification on download (currently only the
  publish-time Ed25519 over manifest+hash is trusted; SHA-256 hash
  check confirms CDN integrity but not authenticity-per-fetch).
- Biometric / device-PIN unlock so the user doesn't re-type their
  password on every cold start (the question they asked earlier
  about "why do I always log in").
- Auto-archive / GC for tombstone bloat.

**UX polish**
- Swipe-to-archive gesture (Material3 SwipeToDismissBox).
- Stacking same-plugin cards within a short time window
  (Gemini's idea from consultation 35).
- Auto-expand the bottom nav on detail screens (Codex's question
  from review 39).

docs\crypto-spec.md:88:> **V1 contract change (M5.1):** previous draft of this spec required `message_id`, `created_at`, and `schema_version` in AAD — those fields are server-generated and unknowable to the sender at signing time, so they have been removed from both AAD and the envelope. They remain server metadata stored next to the message but are not signed by the sender. AAD and the envelope are intentionally distinct: AAD authenticates context to AES-GCM (no ciphertext); the envelope is what Ed25519 signs (AAD + ciphertext + nonce). Replay protection is enforced at the server via the per-sender nonce registry (see §7).
docs\crypto-spec.md:142:aad_json = {"expires_at":"2026-05-20T00:00:00Z","min_plugin_version":"1.0.0","plugin_id":"plugin.weather","sender_id":"sender-alpha","user_id":"user-123"}
docs\crypto-spec.md:148:Ciphertext is verified via round-trip in both `server/tests/test_crypto.py` and `android/core/crypto/.../SpecVectorsTest.kt` rather than via a fixed hex assertion — the ciphertext depends on AAD bytes, and the V1.1 AAD shape is the contract going forward. Old AAD bytes (with `message_id`/`created_at`/`schema_version`) are obsolete.

docs\crypto-spec.md:156:The sender signs the canonical envelope JSON with Ed25519. docs\crypto-spec.md:70:Missing AAD fields are errors. `min_plugin_version` is an empty string when unset (never null). `expires_at` is required and must be a future timestamp ≤ 30 days from the signing instant.
docs\crypto-spec.md:83:  "min_plugin_version": "...",

docs\crypto-spec.md:88:> **V1 contract change (M5.1):** previous draft of this spec required `message_id`, `created_at`, and `schema_version` in AAD — those fields are server-generated and unknowable to the sender at signing time, so they have been removed from both AAD and the envelope. They remain server metadata stored next to the message but are not signed by the sender. AAD and the envelope are intentionally distinct: AAD authenticates context to AES-GCM (no ciphertext); the envelope is what Ed25519 signs (AAD + ciphertext + nonce). Replay protection is enforced at the server via the per-sender nonce registry (see §7).
docs\crypto-spec.md:142:aad_json = {"expires_at":"2026-05-20T00:00:00Z","min_plugin_version":"1.0.0","plugin_id":"plugin.weather","sender_id":"sender-alpha","user_id":"user-123"}
docs\crypto-spec.md:148:Ciphertext is verified via round-trip in both `server/tests/test_crypto.py` and `android/core/crypto/.../SpecVectorsTest.kt` rather than via a fixed hex assertion — the ciphertext depends on AAD bytes, and the V1.1 AAD shape is the contract going forward. Old AAD bytes (with `message_id`/`created_at`/`schema_version`) are obsolete.

docs\crypto-spec.md:156:The sender signs the canonical envelope JSON with Ed25519.   93: async def store_message(

  95:     *,

 119:     # Storage is independent of the push channel. We require at least one
 120:     # non-revoked device so the message has a recipient; devices without an
 121:     # FCM token can still receive it via the /v1/messages/inbox pull endpoint
 122:     # (used in dev builds without google-services.json, and as a fallback for
 123:     # users who declined notification permission). FCM push, when available,
 124:     # is best-effort on top of storage ג€” see push_message_to_user_devices.
 125:     devices = await _active_devices(db, user_id)
 126:     if not devices:
 127:         raise NoActiveDeviceWithPluginError("user has no active devices")
 128: 
 129:     # Encrypted body is opaque to the server; we keep it in a separate blob table or

 141:     )

 160: async def get_message_for_user(
 161:     db: AsyncSession, *, user_id: uuid.UUID, message_id: uuid.UUID
 162: ) -> Message:
 163:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
 164:     result = await db.execute(
 165:         select(Message).where(
 166:             and_(
 167:                 Message.id == message_id,
 168:                 Message.user_id == user_id,
 169:                 Message.expires_at > now,
 170:             ),
 171:         ),
 172:     )
 173:     message = result.scalar_one_or_none()
 174:     if message is None:
 175:         raise MessageNotFoundError(f"message {message_id} not found")

 179: async def inbox_for_device(
 180:     db: AsyncSession,
 181:     *,
 182:     user_id: uuid.UUID,
 183:     device_id: uuid.UUID,
 184:     since: datetime | None,
 185:     limit: int = 50,
 186: ) -> tuple[list[Message], datetime | None]:
 187:     now = datetime.now(UTC)
 188:     query = (
 189:         select(Message)
 190:         .where(
 191:             and_(Message.user_id == user_id, Message.expires_at > now),
 192:         )
 193:         .order_by(Message.sent_at.asc())
 194:         .limit(limit)
 195:     )
 196:     if since is not None:
 197:         query = query.where(Message.sent_at > since)
 198: 
 199:     result = await db.execute(query)
 200:     messages = list(result.scalars().all())
 201:     next_since = messages[-1].sent_at if messages else since
 202:     return messages, next_since

   1: /**
   2:  * Sign a plugin bundle for Syncler.
   3:  *
   4:  * The Android host verifies the signature over
   5:  *   canonical_manifest_without_signature  ||  bundleHash_raw_bytes
   6:  * per ``docs/crypto-spec.md`` ֲ§5. This tool computes the bundle hash,
   7:  * inserts it into the manifest, computes the canonical bytes the same
   8:  * way Android does, signs those, and writes the signature back into
   9:  * the manifest.
  10:  *
  11:  * Usage: tsx tools/sign-bundle.ts <bundle.js> <ed25519_private_key.pem> <manifest.json> [output.signed.json]
  12:  */
  13: import { createHash, sign } from 'node:crypto';
  14: import { readFile, writeFile } from 'node:fs/promises';
  15: import { basename } from 'node:path';
  16: 
  17: interface Manifest {
  18:   bundleHash?: string;
  19:   signature?: string;
  20:   [key: string]: unknown;
  21: }
  22: 
  23: const [, , bundlePath, privateKeyPath, manifestPath, outputPath] = process.argv;
  24: 
  25: if (!bundlePath || !privateKeyPath || !manifestPath) {
  26:   console.error(
  27:     'Usage: tsx tools/sign-bundle.ts <bundle.js> <ed25519_private_key.pem> <manifest.json> [output.signed.json]'
  28:   );
  29:   process.exit(1);
  30: }
  31: 
  32: const bundle = await readFile(bundlePath);
  33: const privateKey = await readFile(privateKeyPath, 'utf8');
  34: const manifest = JSON.parse(await readFile(manifestPath, 'utf8')) as Manifest;
  35: 
  36: const bundleHashHex = createHash('sha256').update(bundle).digest('hex');
  37: const bundleHashBytes = Buffer.from(bundleHashHex, 'hex');
  38: 
  39: // Manifest gets bundleHash inserted before signing; signature field is
  40: // removed (cannot self-include) and the manifest is canonicalized.
  41: const manifestWithBundleHash: Manifest = { ...manifest, bundleHash: bundleHashHex };
  42: delete manifestWithBundleHash.signature;
  43: 
  44: const canonicalManifest = Buffer.from(canonicalJson(manifestWithBundleHash), 'utf8');
  45: const signingInput = Buffer.concat([canonicalManifest, bundleHashBytes]);
  46: 
  47: const signatureHex = sign(null, signingInput, privateKey).toString('hex');
  48: 
  49: const signedManifest = {
  50:   ...manifest,
  51:   bundleHash: bundleHashHex,
  52:   signature: signatureHex,
  53: };
  54: 
  55: const target = outputPath ?? manifestPath.replace(/\.json$/i, '.signed.json');
  56: await writeFile(target, `${JSON.stringify(signedManifest, null, 2)}\n`, 'utf8');
  57: 
  58: console.log(`Signed ${basename(bundlePath)}`);
  59: console.log(`bundleHash=${bundleHashHex}`);
  60: console.log(`manifest=${target}`);
  61: 
  62: /**
  63:  * Canonical JSON with sorted keys, no whitespace, ASCII-escape non-ASCII.
  64:  * Matches ``server/app/crypto/signatures.py:canonical_manifest_for_signing``
  65:  * and ``android/.../PluginSignatureVerifier.kt:canonicalJson`` byte-for-byte
  66:  * given equivalent inputs.
  67:  */
  68: function canonicalJson(value: unknown): string {
  69:   if (value === null) return 'null';
  70:   if (typeof value === 'boolean') return value ? 'true' : 'false';
  71:   if (typeof value === 'number') {
  72:     if (!Number.isFinite(value)) throw new Error('JSON numbers must be finite');
  73:     return Number.isInteger(value) ? String(value) : String(value);
  74:   }
  75:   if (typeof value === 'string') return quote(value);
  76:   if (Array.isArray(value)) {
  77:     return '[' + value.map(canonicalJson).join(',') + ']';
  78:   }
  79:   if (typeof value === 'object') {
  80:     const keys = Object.keys(value as object).sort();
  81:     return (
  82:       '{' +
  83:       keys
  84:         .map((k) => quote(k) + ':' + canonicalJson((value as Record<string, unknown>)[k]))
  85:         .join(',') +
  86:       '}'
  87:     );
  88:   }
  89:   throw new Error(`Unsupported value type: ${typeof value}`);
  90: }
  91: 
  92: function quote(s: string): string {
  93:   let out = '"';
  94:   for (const ch of s) {
  95:     const code = ch.codePointAt(0)!;
  96:     switch (ch) {
  97:       case '"':
  98:         out += '\\"';
  99:         break;
 100:       case '\\':
 101:         out += '\\\\';
 102:         break;
 103:       case '\b':
 104:         out += '\\b';
 105:         break;
 106:       case '\f':
 107:         out += '\\f';
 108:         break;
 109:       case '\n':
 110:         out += '\\n';
 111:         break;
 112:       case '\r':
 113:         out += '\\r';
 114:         break;
 115:       case '\t':
 116:         out += '\\t';
 117:         break;
 118:       default:
 119:         if (code < 0x20 || code > 0x7e) {
 120:           out += '\\u' + code.toString(16).padStart(4, '0');
 121:         } else {
 122:           out += ch;
 123:         }
 124:     }
 125:   }
 126:   return out + '"';
 127: }

 succeeded in 290ms:
# syncler (Python sender SDK)

Send messages from your backend into the Syncler platform.

## Install

```sh
pip install syncler
```

## Quickstart

```python
from syncler import Client

client = Client(
    sender_name="Trading Bot",
    private_key_path="~/.syncler/keys/trading.pem",
    base_url="https://api.syncler.app",
)

# Once: register the sender's public key. Persist the returned sender_id.
sender_id = client.register_if_needed(contact="ops@example.com")
print("Save this:", sender_id)

# Or on subsequent runs:
client.set_sender_id("the-saved-sender-id")

# Pair with a user (one-time per user-device).
qr_path = client.create_pairing_qr(ttl_seconds=300)
print(f"Show this QR to the user: {qr_path}")
# Once the user pairs in their Syncler app, they'll get a confirmation
# screen showing your sender's fingerprint. They confirm. You need their
# user_id + pairing_key from the device-side exchange (M7 wires this; for
# now in dev, use client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key)).

client.set_pairing(user_id="...", pairing_key=b"...32-bytes-shared-secret...")

# Send a message.
result = client.send_to(
    user_uuid=client._latest_pairing.user_id,
    plugin_identifier="com.trading.app",
    plugin_id="row-uuid-of-published-version",
    payload={"pnl": 1234.56, "trades": 7},
    min_plugin_version="1.0.0",
)
print(f"Sent {result.message_id}, expires {result.expires_at}")
```

## Publishing a plugin

```python
import hashlib

bundle_bytes = open("path/to/plugin.bundle.js", "rb").read()
bundle_hash = hashlib.sha256(bundle_bytes).digest()

# manifest_hash is the SHA-256 of the canonical manifest JSON; the
# bundle_signature is the Ed25519 signature over canonical_manifest
# + bundleHash bytes (see docs/crypto-spec.md ֲ§5).
response = client.publish_plugin(
    plugin_identifier="com.trading.app",
    version="1.0.0",
    manifest_hash=manifest_hash,
    bundle_hash=bundle_hash,
    bundle_signature=bundle_signature,
    signed_bundle_url="https://your-cdn.com/plugin.bundle.js",
    capabilities=["network"],
    endpoints=["https://your-backend.com/api/*"],
)
print("Published version row:", response["plugin_row_id"])
```

## Threading

The client is sync. Wrap calls in your own thread pool / asyncio executor
if you need concurrent sends.

## Spec

See `docs/crypto-spec.md` (top of repo) for the canonical AAD + envelope
shapes. The SDK is the reference Python implementation.

## 6. Sending a card (your backend, per event)

  15: 
  16: ### What the host does for you
  17: 
  18: Once a card is in a user's inbox, the host handles all of the following without you doing anything plugin-side:
  19: 
  20: - **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary / timestamp).
  21: - **Unread indicator** + read sync across the user's devices. A row marks read when the user opens the detail view; the state syncs via an encrypted CAS state blob.
  22: - **Date buckets** in the chronological view (Today / Yesterday / Earlier).
  23: - **Group-by-sender** toggle with collapsible sections ג€” the user picks chronological or grouped from the top app bar.
  24: - **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
  25: - **Archive** + **Delete** + **Multi-select** with bulk Archive / Delete. Archive/delete state is local and synced across devices; deleted messages are hidden from inbox AND archive.
  26: - **Bottom navigation** (Inbox / Senders / Settings) ג€” the user is always one tap away from your card.
  27: - **Revocation UX** ג€” if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See ֲ§5.5.
  28: 
  29: You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.
  30: 
  31: ## 2. Protocol
  32: 
  33: ### Payload (your backend ג†’ user device)
  34: 
  35: Two parts: a reserved **`hostPreview`** block the platform renders natively as the inbox row, and the rest of the payload that your plugin's `render()` consumes for the detail view.
 115:     dismissBehavior: DismissBehavior.DISMISS_ALL,
 116:     minPlatformVersion: '1.0.0',
 117:   };
 118: 
 119:   // onMessage is NOT invoked in V1 inbox mode ג€” message arrival is already
 120:   // surfaced by the host-rendered row from hostPreview. If you implement it
 121:   // anyway, do not call platform.showNotification (rejects in V1).
 122:   // The host will invoke onMessage when the V1.5 OS-notification path ships.
 123: 
 124:   render(payload: MyPayload): string {
 125:     // V1 recommended pattern: button handler calls `platform.network.fetch`
 126:     // directly. The `platform.message.respond` + `onAction` round-trip is
 127:     // reserved for V1.5 (it lets the platform sync action state across
 128:     // devices). For V1, post directly to your declared endpoint.
 129:     return `
 130:       <div style="font-family:sans-serif;padding:16px">
 131:         <h2>${escapeHtml(payload.hostPreview.title)}</h2>
 132:         <p>${escapeHtml(payload.body)}</p>
 133:         <button id="act" style="font-size:18px;padding:12px">${escapeHtml(payload.action_label)}</button>
 134:       </div>
 135:       <script>
 136:         const itemId = ${JSON.stringify(payload.item_id)};
 137:         document.getElementById('act').onclick = async () => {
 138:           await platform.network.fetch('https://your-app.example.com/api/action', {
 139:             method: 'POST',
 140:             headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
 141:             body: JSON.stringify({
 142:               item_id: itemId,
 143:               acted_at: new Date().toISOString(),
 144:             }),
 145:           });
 146:           document.getElementById('act').textContent = 'Sent';
 147:         };
 148:       </script>
 149:     `;
 150:   }
 151: }
 152: 
 153: // Required: self-register at bundle load. Without this call the host's
 154: // dispatcher has no plugin to dispatch into, and you'll see a "missing
 155: // registerPlugin() call?" error in the card.
 156: registerPlugin(new MyPlugin());
 157: ```
 158: 
 159: Render whatever HTML/CSS/JS suits your domain. The WebView is isolated; only `platform.*` APIs cross the boundary.
 160: 
 161: **V1 card-render bridge ג€” what's wired:**
 162: - `platform.network.fetch(url, init)` ג€” works, gated by `declaredEndpoints` glob match
 163: - `platform.showNotification`, `platform.storage`, `platform.camera`, `platform.gallery`, `platform.file`, `platform.location`, `platform.message.respond` ג€” *reject* with a clear error in V1 inbox mode. The full bridge needs the multi-process plugin host and is a follow-up. For V1 dogfood, stick to network.fetch.
 164: 
 165: ## 4. Build + sign the plugin
 166: 
 167: ```sh
 168: # Install the SDK
 169: cd my-plugin
 170: npm install @syncler/plugin-sdk
 220:     endpoints=["https://your-app.example.com/api/*"],
 221: )
 222: 
 223: print("Published row:", response["plugin_row_id"])
 224: # Save this ג€” you'll need it in `send_to(plugin_id=...)`.
 225: ```
 226: 
 227: ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 228: 
 229: If a published bundle is found to be buggy or compromised, you should revoke it immediately. This prevents new messages from using that bundle and allows the host to render appropriate security warnings for messages already in users' inboxes.
 230: 
 231: ```python
 232: client.revoke_plugin(
 233:     plugin_row_id="<the-uuid-from-publish_plugin>",
 234:     reason="compromised",  # optional: superseded, compromised, sender_disabled
 235: )
 236: ```
 237: 
 238: **Classification and UX:**
 239: 
 240: | Reason | Severity | Host UX |
 241: |---|---|---|
 242: | `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
 243: | `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
 244: | `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
 245: | `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
 246: 
 247: Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` ג†’ `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
 248: 
 249: ## 6. Sending a card (your backend, per event)
 250: 
 251: ```python
 252: # After pairing ג€” see SDK README for the pairing dance.
 253: client.set_pairing(user_id="...", pairing_key=b"...32-bytes...")
 254: 
 255: result = client.send_to(
 280: Content-Type: application/json
 281: 
 282: { "item_id": "...", "acted_at": "..." }
 283: ```
 284: 
 285: Note: the platform does **not** inject `device_id` into the body for you in V1. If you need to distinguish which device acted, include a sender-generated identifier in your payload and have the plugin echo it back. Dedupe by `item_id` alone if a single tap is what you care about.
 286: 
 287: - Status 200 -> recorded.
 288: - Status 409 -> idempotent dedupe (already saw this item); platform may retry on transient network errors so be ready.
 289: - Status 4xx other -> platform surfaces a generic failure to the plugin's promise.
 290: 
 291: ```python
 292: # Flask example ג€” dedupe by item_id alone in V1.
 293: @app.post("/api/action")
 294: def action():
 295:     data = request.json
 296:     item_id = data["item_id"]
 297:     if Action.query.filter_by(item_id=item_id).first():
 298:         return "", 409
 299:     db.session.add(Action(item_id=item_id, acted_at=data["acted_at"]))
 300:     db.session.commit()
 301:     return "", 200
 302: ```
 303: 
 304: ## 8. Testing it end-to-end
 305: 
 306: 1. Install the Syncler Android app (`./gradlew :app:installDebug`).
 307: 2. Sign up + log in. The app auto-enrolls this device with the server.
 308: 3. From your backend, run a script that registers your sender and prints a pairing QR (see SDK README).
 309: 4. Tap **Pair sender** ג†’ **Scan QR** in the Syncler app. Confirm the fingerprint matches what your script prints.
 310: 5. After confirming, the app shows your `user_id` and a `pairing_key_hex`. Copy both and feed them into your backend's `client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key=bytes.fromhex(...))` so it can encrypt for you. (V1 dev-mode handoff; V1.5 will wire this automatically via the bootstrap exchange.)
 311: 6. Publish your plugin (`client.publish_plugin(...)`) ג€” save the `plugin_row_id`.
 312: 7. Run `client.send_to(...)` with a test payload.
 313: 8. Within ~15s the phone's inbox poll picks it up, decrypts, fetches your bundle, and renders the card in a WebView.
 314: 9. Tap your action button on the phone.
 315: 10. Confirm your `/api/action` endpoint received the POST.

 317: ## 9. Common errors
 318: 
 319: - **`401 invalid envelope signature`** ג€” your sender's Ed25519 key doesn't match the one registered. Re-check `private_key_path`.
 320: - **`410 plugin missing, revoked, or not owned by sender`** ג€” `plugin_id` (the row UUID) is wrong, or you accidentally used `plugin_identifier`. The two are distinct (see ֲ§5 vs ֲ§6).
 321: - **`410 recipient has no active devices`** ג€” the user has no enrolled device (signed up but never opened the app, or revoked all devices). FCM availability is *not* required; messages are stored regardless and pulled via `/v1/messages/inbox`.
 322: - **`409 nonce already used`** ג€” your code reused a nonce somehow; SDK generates fresh nonces per `send_to`, so this means you're calling `send_to` with cached envelope bytes. Rebuild.
 323: - **`429 rate limited`** ג€” back off + retry per `Retry-After` header.
 324: - **Card shows "render failed: plugin did not install __syncler_internal_dispatch ג€” missing registerPlugin() call?"** ג€” your bundle defined the plugin class but didn't call `registerPlugin(new YourPlugin())` at module scope. See ֲ§3.
 325: - **Card shows "endpoint not declared"** ג€” your `onclick` handler is calling a URL that doesn't match any pattern in your manifest's `declaredEndpoints`. Add the URL pattern (globs allowed: `https://example.com/api/*`) and re-publish.
 326: - **`HostPreviewValidationError: hostPreview.X is N UTF-8 bytes; max is M`** ג€” caught at `client.send_to` time. Trim the offending field; see ֲ§2 for the caps. UTF-8 byte counts, not characters ג€” emoji and accented characters cost more than one byte.
 327: - **Row shows "New message from {sender}" with fallback text only** ג€” your message was sent without a `hostPreview` block, or the block was malformed (logged + ignored on the device). The detail view still loads the plugin and renders normally; only the row is generic. Add a valid `hostPreview` and re-send.
 328: 
 329: Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.
 330: 
 331: ## 10. Versioning + history
 332: 
 333: Syncler provides a **bundle-by-hash guarantee**. When you send a message, it is bound to the specific `plugin_id` (row UUID) you supplied at send-time.
 334: 
 335: 1.  **Immutability:** Each message in a user's inbox resolves to the exact JS bundle version it was originally validated against. 
 336: 2.  **Safety:** You can publish `v2.0.0` with breaking changes to your `render()` logic without breaking the display of `v1.0.0` messages already in users' inboxes. The host fetches the correct historical bundle via the `/v1/plugins/by-id/{id}` endpoint.
 337: 3.  **Caching:** The host caches these bundles by their SHA-256 hash. In the current version, this cache is in-memory; an app restart may trigger a re-fetch of historical bundles. Persistent disk-based bundle storage is a V1.5 optimization.
 338: 
 339: If you need to retract a version for security reasons, use `revoke_plugin` with the `compromised` reason (ֲ§5.5).
 340: 
 341: ---

**Classification and UX:**

| Reason | Severity | Host UX |
|---|---|---|
| `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
| `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |

Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` ג†’ `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.

 ## 4. Build + sign the plugin
 
@@ -226,25 +224,25 @@
 
 ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 
-If a published bundle is found to be buggy or compromised, you should revoke it immediately. This prevents new messages from using that bundle and allows the host to render appropriate security warnings for messages already in users' inboxes.
+Revoke a single published plugin row when that exact version should no longer be treated as active:
 
 ```python
 client.revoke_plugin(
-    plugin_row_id="<the-uuid-from-publish_plugin>",
-    reason="compromised",  # optional: superseded, compromised, sender_disabled
+    plugin_row_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
+    reason="superseded",
 )
 ```
 
-**Classification and UX:**
+`reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 
-| Reason | Severity | Host UX |
+| Reason | Use when | Host UX |
 |---|---|---|
-| `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
-| `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
-| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
-| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
+| `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
+| `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 
-Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` → `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
+The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

 ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 
-If a published bundle is found to be buggy or compromised, you should revoke it immediately. This prevents new messages from using that bundle and allows the host to render appropriate security warnings for messages already in users' inboxes.
+Revoke a single published plugin row when that exact version should no longer be treated as active:
 
 ```python
 client.revoke_plugin(
-    plugin_row_id="<the-uuid-from-publish_plugin>",
-    reason="compromised",  # optional: superseded, compromised, sender_disabled
+    plugin_row_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
+    reason="superseded",
 )
 ```
 
-**Classification and UX:**
+`reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 
-| Reason | Severity | Host UX |
+| Reason | Use when | Host UX |
 |---|---|---|
-| `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
-| `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
-| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
-| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
+| `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
+| `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 
-Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` → `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
+The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

 ## 4. Build + sign the plugin
 
@@ -226,25 +224,25 @@
 
 ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 
-If a published bundle is found to be buggy or compromised, you should revoke it immediately. This prevents new messages from using that bundle and allows the host to render appropriate security warnings for messages already in users' inboxes.
+Revoke a single published plugin row when that exact version should no longer be treated as active:
 
 ```python
 client.revoke_plugin(
-    plugin_row_id="<the-uuid-from-publish_plugin>",
-    reason="compromised",  # optional: superseded, compromised, sender_disabled
+    plugin_row_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
+    reason="superseded",
 )
 ```
 
-**Classification and UX:**
+`reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 
-| Reason | Severity | Host UX |
+| Reason | Use when | Host UX |
 |---|---|---|
-| `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
-| `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
-| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
-| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
+| `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
+| `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 
-Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` → `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
+The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

 ## 9. Common errors
@@ -330,15 +330,16 @@
 
 ## 10. Versioning + history
 
-Syncler provides a **bundle-by-hash guarantee**. When you send a message, it is bound to the specific `plugin_id` (row UUID) you supplied at send-time.
+Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
+
+Version strings use semver-lite: `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH` with an optional prerelease suffix. Each numeric component is capped at 6 digits, and every publish for the same `(sender_id, plugin_identifier)` must be strictly greater than all existing versions.
+
+When you send a card, pass the exact `plugin_row_id` that matches the payload schema you produced. The message stores that row UUID. On the device, Syncler resolves the historical row by ID, not by `/latest`, so a v1 message keeps using the v1 bundle even after you publish v2.
 
-1.  **Immutability:** Each message in a user's inbox resolves to the exact JS bundle version it was originally validated against. 
-2.  **Safety:** You can publish `v2.0.0` with breaking changes to your `render()` logic without breaking the display of `v1.0.0` messages already in users' inboxes. The host fetches the correct historical bundle via the `/v1/plugins/by-id/{id}` endpoint.
-3.  **Caching:** The host caches these bundles by their SHA-256 hash. In the current version, this cache is in-memory; an app restart may trigger a re-fetch of historical bundles. Persistent disk-based bundle storage is a V1.5 optimization.
+The device verifies the downloaded bundle against the row's SHA-256 `bundle_hash` and caches verified bundle bytes by hash for the process lifetime. On app restart, the cache is empty and the device re-fetches the same historical row's `signed_bundle_url`. Keep old bundle URLs available for as long as you want old inbox messages to remain renderable.
 
-If you need to retract a version for security reasons, use `revoke_plugin` with the `compromised` reason (§5.5).
+Archive/delete are user-organization states synced through the encrypted user-state blob. They do not remove the server copy, and archive does not store a local message body beyond the server's retention window.

 ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 
-If a published bundle is found to be buggy or compromised, you should revoke it immediately. This prevents new messages from using that bundle and allows the host to render appropriate security warnings for messages already in users' inboxes.
+Revoke a single published plugin row when that exact version should no longer be treated as active:
 
 ```python
 client.revoke_plugin(
-    plugin_row_id="<the-uuid-from-publish_plugin>",
-    reason="compromised",  # optional: superseded, compromised, sender_disabled
+    plugin_row_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
+    reason="superseded",
 )
 ```
 
-**Classification and UX:**
+`reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 
-| Reason | Severity | Host UX |
+| Reason | Use when | Host UX |
 |---|---|---|
-| `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
-| `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
-| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
-| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
+| `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
+| `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 
-Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` → `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
+The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

 ## 10. Versioning + history
 
-Syncler provides a **bundle-by-hash guarantee**. When you send a message, it is bound to the specific `plugin_id` (row UUID) you supplied at send-time.
+Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
+
+Version strings use semver-lite: `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH` with an optional prerelease suffix. Each numeric component is capped at 6 digits, and every publish for the same `(sender_id, plugin_identifier)` must be strictly greater than all existing versions.
 
-1.  **Immutability:** Each message in a user's inbox resolves to the exact JS bundle version it was originally validated against. 
-2.  **Safety:** You can publish `v2.0.0` with breaking changes to your `render()` logic without breaking the display of `v1.0.0` messages already in users' inboxes. The host fetches the correct historical bundle via the `/v1/plugins/by-id/{id}` endpoint.
-3.  **Caching:** The host caches these bundles by their SHA-256 hash. In the current version, this cache is in-memory; an app restart may trigger a re-fetch of historical bundles. Persistent disk-based bundle storage is a V1.5 optimization.
+When you send a card, pass the exact `plugin_row_id` that matches the payload schema you produced. The message stores that row UUID. On the device, Syncler resolves the historical row by ID, not by `/latest`, so a v1 message keeps using the v1 bundle even after you publish v2.
+
+The device verifies the downloaded bundle against the row's SHA-256 `bundle_hash` and caches verified bundle bytes by hash for the process lifetime. On app restart, the cache is empty and the device re-fetches the same historical row's `signed_bundle_url`. Keep old bundle URLs available for as long as you want old inbox messages to remain renderable.
 
-If you need to retract a version for security reasons, use `revoke_plugin` with the `compromised` reason (§5.5).
+Archive/delete are user-organization states synced through the encrypted user-state blob. They do not remove the server copy, and archive does not store a local message body beyond the server's retention window.

+### What the host does for you
+
+Once a card is in a user's inbox, the host handles all of the following without you doing anything plugin-side:
+
+- **Native row rendering** from your `hostPreview` block (title / subtitle / summary / timestamp).
+- **Unread indicator** + read sync across the user's devices. A row marks read when the user opens the detail view; the state syncs via an encrypted CAS state blob.
+- **Date buckets** in the chronological view (Today / Yesterday / Earlier).
+- **Group-by-sender** toggle with collapsible sections — the user picks chronological or grouped from the top app bar.
+- **Inbox search** (case-insensitive substring) over title, subtitle, summary, sender name, AND any tokens you supplied in `hostPreview.searchText`.
+- **Archive** + **Delete** + **Multi-select** with bulk Archive / Delete. Archive/delete state is local and synced across devices; deleted messages are hidden from inbox AND archive. The server retains messages until their normal expiry.
+- **Bottom navigation** (Inbox / Senders / Settings) — the user is always one tap away from your card.
+- **Revocation UX** — if you revoke a plugin version with a `compromised` reason, the host refuses to execute the bundle on the device and shows a security banner instead. See §5.5.
+
+You don't need to opt into any of these. Populate `hostPreview` and they all work.

+5. After confirming, the app shows your `user_id` and a `pairing_key_hex`. Copy both and feed them into your backend's `client.set_pairing(user_id, pairing_key=bytes.fromhex(...))` so it can encrypt for you.
 6. Publish your plugin (`client.publish_plugin(...)`) — save the `plugin_row_id`.
 7. Run `client.send_to(...)` with a test payload.
-8. Within ~15s the phone's inbox poll picks it up, decrypts, fetches your bundle, and renders the card in a WebView.

+8. Within ~15s the phone's inbox poll picks it up, decrypts it, fetches your bundle, and shows the native inbox row.
+9. Tap the row to open the plugin-rendered detail view, then tap your action button.
 10. Confirm your `/api/action` endpoint received the POST.
 
 ## 9. Common errors
@@ -291,6 +328,18 @@ def action():
 
 Cross-reference `docs/crypto-spec.md` for the AAD + envelope canonical byte shapes if signatures disagree.
 
+## 10. Versioning + history
+
+Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
+
+Version strings use semver-lite: `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH` with an optional prerelease suffix. Each numeric component is capped at 6 digits, and every publish for the same `(sender_id, plugin_identifier)` must be strictly greater than all existing versions.
+
+When you send a card, pass the exact `plugin_row_id` that matches the payload schema you produced. The message stores that row UUID. On the device, Syncler resolves the historical row by ID, not by `/latest`, so a v1 message keeps using the v1 bundle even after you publish v2.
+
+The device verifies the downloaded bundle against the row's SHA-256 `bundle_hash` and caches verified bundle bytes by hash for the process lifetime. On app restart, the cache is empty and the device re-fetches the same historical row's `signed_bundle_url`. Keep old bundle URLs available for as long as you want old inbox messages to remain renderable.
+
+Archive/delete are user-organization states synced through the encrypted user-state blob. They do not remove the server copy, and archive does not store a local message body beyond the server's retention window.
+
 ---
 
-**Six pages.** If you needed more than that to integrate, the SDK has a DX problem — file a finding back at the Syncler team.
+**Seven pages.** If you needed more than that to integrate, the SDK has a DX problem — file a finding back at the Syncler team.

@@ -226,25 +224,25 @@
 
 ### 5.5 Revoking a plugin version
 
-If a published bundle is found to be buggy or compromised, you should revoke it immediately. This prevents new messages from using that bundle and allows the host to render appropriate security warnings for messages already in users' inboxes.
+Revoke a single published plugin row when that exact version should no longer be treated as active:
 
 ```python
 client.revoke_plugin(
-    plugin_row_id="<the-uuid-from-publish_plugin>",
-    reason="compromised",  # optional: superseded, compromised, sender_disabled
+    plugin_row_id="<plugin_row_id from publish_plugin>",
+    reason="superseded",
 )
 ```
 
-**Classification and UX:**
+`reason` is optional for legacy compatibility, but senders should always supply one of:
 
-| Reason | Severity | Host UX |
+| Reason | Use when | Host UX |
 |---|---|---|
-| `superseded` | Low | Silent. The version is inactive for new messages, but existing inbox cards render normally. |
-| `compromised` | High | **Refusal to execute.** The host renders a red security banner and will not load the bundle. The raw decrypted payload is shown for diagnostic purposes. |
-| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
-| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
+| `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
+| `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 
-Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` → `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
+The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

 ## 10. Versioning + history
 
-Syncler provides a **bundle-by-hash guarantee**. When you send a message, it is bound to the specific `plugin_id` (row UUID) you supplied at send-time.

-2.  **Safety:** You can publish `v2.0.0` with breaking changes to your `render()` logic without breaking the display of `v1.0.0` messages already in users' inboxes. The host fetches the correct historical bundle via the `/v1/plugins/by-id/{id}` endpoint.

-| `sender_disabled` | Medium | Neutral banner. The host renders an "Unavailable" notice in the detail view but still allows the bundle to execute so historical cards remain readable. |
-| `unspecified` | Medium | Fallback for legacy revokes. Renders like `sender_disabled`. |
+| `superseded` | A newer version replaces this row. | Shows a subdued "newer version available" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `compromised` | The bundle or signing key is unsafe. | Refuses to execute the bundle and shows a security banner with the decrypted payload fallback. |
+| `sender_disabled` | The sender/service is intentionally disabled. | Shows a neutral "sender unavailable" banner in detail; the historical bundle can still render. |
+| `unspecified` | You are migrating legacy tooling and cannot classify the revoke. | Shows a generic revoked banner; avoid using this for new revokes. |
 
-Revocation reasons are monotone: you can "upgrade" a reason (e.g., `superseded` → `compromised`) if new information surfaces, but downgrades are ignored. The reason is part of the signed envelope and cannot be stripped by a third party.
+The revoke request is signed by the SDK. The `reason` value is included in the signed envelope, so an intermediary cannot strip `compromised` down to a softer classification. Re-revoking a row keeps the original `revoked_at`; a higher-severity reason can promote the row, while downgrades are ignored.

 ## 10. Versioning + history
 
-Syncler provides a **bundle-by-hash guarantee**. When you send a message, it is bound to the specific `plugin_id` (row UUID) you supplied at send-time.
+Publish every plugin release as a new row under the same `plugin_identifier`. `plugin_identifier` is the stable name, while `plugin_row_id` is the exact version row returned by `client.publish_plugin(...)`.
 
-1.  **Immutability:** Each message in a user's inbox resolves to the exact JS bundle version it was originally validated against. 
-2.  **Safety:** You can publish `v2.0.0` with breaking changes to your `render()` logic without breaking the display of `v1.0.0` messages already in users' inboxes. The host fetches the correct historical bundle via the `/v1/plugins/by-id/{id}` endpoint.
-3.  **Caching:** The host caches these bundles by their SHA-256 hash. In the current version, this cache is in-memory; an app restart may trigger a re-fetch of historical bundles. Persistent disk-based bundle storage is a V1.5 optimization.
+Version strings use semver-lite: `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH` with an optional prerelease suffix. Each numeric component is capped at 6 digits, and every publish for the same `(sender_id, plugin_identifier)` must be strictly greater than all existing versions.
 
-If you need to retract a version for security reasons, use `revoke_plugin` with the `compromised` reason (§5.5).
+When you send a card, pass the exact `plugin_row_id` that matches the payload schema you produced. The message stores that row UUID. On the device, Syncler resolves the historical row by ID, not by `/latest`, so a v1 message keeps using the v1 bundle even after you publish v2.
 
----
+The device verifies the downloaded bundle against the row's SHA-256 `bundle_hash` and caches verified bundle bytes by hash for the process lifetime. On app restart, the cache is empty and the device re-fetches the same historical row's `signed_bundle_url`. Keep old bundle URLs available for as long as you want old inbox messages to remain renderable.
 
-**Six pages.** If you needed more than that to integrate, the SDK has a DX problem — file a finding back at the Syncler team.
+Archive/delete are user-organization states synced through the encrypted user-state blob. They do not remove the server copy, and archive does not store a local message body beyond the server's retention window.

+**Seven pages.** If you needed more than that to integrate, the SDK has a DX problem — file a finding back at the Syncler team.
